# 08 — Source Code Index

## Overview

- **Total PHP files**: 138 (73 application + 65 third-party)
- **Total SQL files**: 246 (2 schema + 244 migrations)
- **Total JS files**: ~11 application + hundreds of library files
- **Total CSS files**: 7 application
- **Base path**: `source-repos/ttrss-php/`

## Entry Points

| File | Purpose | Spec Refs |
|------|---------|-----------|
| `ttrss/index.php` | Web UI entry (HTML bootstrap) | 00-arch, 02-api |
| `ttrss/backend.php` | AJAX RPC dispatcher | 02-api |
| `ttrss/api/index.php` | REST API endpoint | 02-api |
| `ttrss/public.php` | Public feeds/login | 02-api |
| `ttrss/update.php` | CLI update tool | 06-cache |

**Tool Call: Write specs/09\-migration\-dimensions.md**
Status: Completed

Diff: /Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/specs/09-migration-dimensions.md

# 09 — Migration Dimensions Analysis

## Purpose

This document defines the **analysis dimensions** for driving the PHP→Python migration, and proposes **multi-dimensional migration flow variants** to be discussed and selected before starting the actual migration work.

## Analysis Dimensions

### Dimension 1: Call Graph Dependencies

The call graph captures which files/functions call which other files/functions. This determines the **compilation order** — you can't migrate a function until its dependencies exist.

#### Key Dependency Chains

```
Entry Points → Bootstrap → Handlers → Business Logic → Database
                                    → Plugin System
                                    → Feed Processing
```

**Core bootstrap chain** (must be migrated first in any flow):
```
autoload.php → config.php → db.php → sessions.php → functions.php → db-prefs.php
```

**Handler dependency chain**:
```
Handler (base) → Handler_Protected → {RPC, Feeds, Article, Pref_*}
              → Handler_Public
              → API
```

**Feed processing chain**:
```
rssfuncs.php → functions.php → db.php
             → FeedParser → FeedItem_Common → FeedItem_Atom / FeedItem_RSS
             → FeedEnclosure
             → ccache.php → labels.php
```

#### Call Graph Communities (candidates for NetworkX + Leiden detection)

| Community | Files | Description |
|-----------|-------|-------------|
| **Core** | functions.php, functions2.php, db.php, sessions.php, autoload.php | Foundation — everything depends on this |
| **Feed Engine** | rssfuncs.php, feedparser.php, feeditem/*.php, ccache.php | Feed update pipeline |
| **User Interface** | feeds.php, article.php, rpc.php, dlg.php + JS files | Frontend-serving handlers |
| **Preferences** | pref/*.php, db-prefs.php | User/admin settings |
| **Plugin** | pluginhost.php, plugin.php, pluginhandler.php | Extension system |
| **API** | api.php, api/index.php | External API |
| **Auth** | sessions.php, auth/base.php, iauthmodule.php, auth_internal | Authentication |
| **Infrastructure** | logger/*.php, dbupdater.php, ttrssmailer.php, crypt.php | Cross-cutting services |

### Dimension 2: Entity / Database Relationships

The entity dimension maps source code to the database tables it operates on. This determines which **data models** need to exist before business logic can be migrated.

#### Entity Clusters

| Cluster | Tables | Operating Code |
|---------|--------|----------------|
| **User Core** | ttrss_users, ttrss_sessions, ttrss_access_keys | sessions.php, functions.php (auth), auth_internal |
| **Feed Management** | ttrss_feeds, ttrss_feed_categories, ttrss_archived_feeds | pref/feeds.php, rssfuncs.php, feeds.php |
| **Article Content** | ttrss_entries, ttrss_user_entries, ttrss_enclosures, ttrss_entry_comments | rssfuncs.php, article.php, feeds.php, functions2.php |
| **Tagging & Labels** | ttrss_tags, ttrss_labels2, ttrss_user_labels2 | labels.php, article.php, rpc.php |
| **Filtering** | ttrss_filters2, ttrss_filters2_rules, ttrss_filters2_actions, ttrss_filter_types, ttrss_filter_actions | pref/filters.php, rssfuncs.php |
| **Preferences** | ttrss_prefs, ttrss_user_prefs, ttrss_prefs_types, ttrss_prefs_sections, ttrss_settings_profiles | db-prefs.php, pref/prefs.php |
| **Caching** | ttrss_counters_cache, ttrss_cat_counters_cache, ttrss_feedbrowser_cache | ccache.php, feedbrowser.php |
| **Plugin** | ttrss_plugin_storage | pluginhost.php |
| **System** | ttrss_version, ttrss_themes, ttrss_error_log | dbupdater.php, logger/sql.php |
| **Federation** | ttrss_linked_instances, ttrss_linked_feeds | (minimal code — low priority) |

#### Entity Dependency Order

```
Level 0 (no FK deps):  ttrss_prefs_types, ttrss_prefs_sections, ttrss_filter_types,
                        ttrss_filter_actions, ttrss_themes, ttrss_version, ttrss_entries

Level 1 (depends on L0): ttrss_users, ttrss_prefs, ttrss_linked_instances

Level 2 (depends on L1): ttrss_feeds, ttrss_feed_categories, ttrss_sessions,
                          ttrss_settings_profiles, ttrss_access_keys, ttrss_labels2,
                          ttrss_filters2, ttrss_user_prefs, ttrss_plugin_storage,
                          ttrss_error_log, ttrss_linked_feeds

Level 3 (depends on L2): ttrss_user_entries, ttrss_archived_feeds,
                          ttrss_filters2_rules, ttrss_filters2_actions,
                          ttrss_counters_cache, ttrss_cat_counters_cache

Level 4 (depends on L3): ttrss_tags, ttrss_user_labels2, ttrss_enclosures,
                          ttrss_entry_comments, ttrss_feedbrowser_cache
```

### Dimension 3: Frontend / Backend Coupling

This dimension maps which backend code serves which frontend components.

| Frontend Component | JS File(s) | Backend Handler(s) | Coupling Level |
|-------------------|------------|---------------------|----------------|
| Feed sidebar tree | FeedTree.js, feedlist.js | Pref_Feeds::getfeedtree, RPC::getAllCounters | HIGH — custom Dojo store |
| Headlines panel | viewfeed.js | Feeds::view (server-rendered HTML) | HIGH — HTML fragments |
| Article view | viewfeed.js | Article::view | MEDIUM — JSON data |
| Preferences | prefs.js, PrefFeed/Filter/LabelTree.js | Pref_* handlers | HIGH — server HTML + Dojo stores |
| Dialogs | functions.js | Dlg, various handlers | HIGH — server HTML |
| Toolbar/actions | tt-rss.js | RPC::mark/publ/delete/archive | LOW — simple JSON |
| Search | viewfeed.js | Feeds::search | MEDIUM |
| API | (external clients) | API class | LOW — pure JSON |

### Dimension 4: Coupling / Cohesion Quality

| Component | Cohesion | Coupling | Assessment |
|-----------|----------|----------|------------|
| `functions.php` | LOW (kitchen sink) | HIGH (everything imports it) | Split into modules by domain |
| `functions2.php` | LOW (continuation of above) | HIGH | Split into modules by domain |
| Handler classes | MEDIUM (grouped by feature) | MEDIUM (share DB, session) | Good migration units |
| Database adapters | HIGH (single responsibility) | LOW (via interface) | Clean migration |
| Feed parser | HIGH (parsing only) | LOW | Clean migration |
| Plugin system | HIGH | LOW (hook-based) | Migrate as unit |
| Session/auth | MEDIUM | HIGH (session globals) | Refactor during migration |

### Dimension 5: Complexity Hotspots

Files ranked by migration complexity (considering size, coupling, and criticality):

| Rank | File | Why Complex |
|------|------|-------------|
| 1 | `include/functions.php` | 2000+ lines, core of everything, auth + config + utils |
| 2 | `include/functions2.php` | 2500+ lines, query building, HTML rendering, search |
| 3 | `include/rssfuncs.php` | 1300+ lines, feed engine, daemon logic |
| 4 | `classes/feeds.php` | 38KB, server-rendered HTML, complex queries |
| 5 | `classes/api.php` | 22KB, must maintain backward compatibility |
| 6 | `classes/rpc.php` | 15KB, state mutations, counter updates |
| 7 | `classes/pluginhost.php` | Cross-cutting, singleton, design decision |
| 8 | `classes/pref/feeds.php` | Complex tree building, batch operations |
| 9 | `classes/pref/filters.php` | Complex rule/action CRUD |
| 10 | `include/sessions.php` | Security-critical, session validation |

### Dimension 6: PHP-Specific Patterns Requiring Translation

| PHP Pattern | Python Equivalent | Affected Files |
|-------------|-------------------|----------------|
| `$_SESSION` globals | Flask session / Django middleware | 50+ files |
| `$_REQUEST` superglobal | `request.args` / `request.form` | All handlers |
| `include_once` / `require_once` | Python `import` | All files |
| `__autoload()` | Python module system (automatic) | autoload.php |
| `$this->dbh->query("SQL...")` | SQLAlchemy session.execute() | 200+ locations |
| `db_escape_string()` | Parameterized queries (automatic) | 200+ locations |
| `json_encode()` / `json_decode()` | `json.dumps()` / `json.loads()` | Many handlers |
| `preg_match()` / `preg_replace()` | `re.match()` / `re.sub()` | functions*.php |
| `htmlspecialchars()` | Jinja2 auto-escape | Many handlers |
| `date()` / `strtotime()` | `datetime` module | Many files |
| Singleton pattern | Module-level instance or dependency injection | Db, PluginHost |
| PHP error handler | Python logging + exception handling | errorhandler.php |

---

## Migration Flow Variants

### Variant A: Entity-First (Bottom-Up)

**Strategy**: Migrate database models first, then build business logic on top.

```
Pass 1: SQLAlchemy models + Alembic migrations (all 35 tables)
Pass 2: Database access layer (repository pattern or direct ORM)
Pass 3: Core utilities (config, auth, session, preferences)
Pass 4: Feed engine (parser, updater, cache)
Pass 5: API handlers (RPC, Feeds, Article, Pref_*)
Pass 6: Plugin system
Pass 7: Frontend adaptation (or keep existing)
Pass 8: Deployment (Docker, CI/CD)
```

**Pros**:
- Clean foundation — models drive everything
- Can validate schema early with real data
- Natural for SQLAlchemy-centric development

**Cons**:
- Long time before any runnable code
- Hard to test without handlers
- Models may need revision when business logic reveals patterns

### Variant B: Call-Graph-First (Top-Down)

**Strategy**: Migrate along the call graph, starting from entry points and working inward.

```
Pass 1: Entry points + bootstrap (Flask app, config, routing)
Pass 2: Handler base classes + dispatch logic
Pass 3: Core handlers (Feeds, Article, RPC) with stub DB
Pass 4: Database layer (replace stubs with real ORM)
Pass 5: Feed engine
Pass 6: Preference handlers
Pass 7: Plugin system
Pass 8: Polish + deployment
```

**Pros**:
- Runnable skeleton early
- Natural for agile/incremental development
- Can use stubs to test routing before DB is ready

**Cons**:
- Stub management overhead
- May need to refactor handlers when DB layer solidifies
- Risk of building on wrong abstractions

### Variant C: Vertical Slice (Feature-First)

**Strategy**: Migrate complete vertical slices — one feature at a time, including its models, logic, API, and frontend.

```
Slice 1: Auth + Users (models + session + login + user mgmt)
Slice 2: Feeds + Categories (models + CRUD + display)
Slice 3: Articles + Headlines (models + view + mark/star)
Slice 4: Feed Update Engine (parser + daemon + cache)
Slice 5: Labels + Tags (models + CRUD + assignment)
Slice 6: Filters (models + rules + actions)
Slice 7: Preferences + Profiles
Slice 8: Plugin System
Slice 9: API (external)
Slice 10: Deployment
```

**Pros**:
- Each slice is testable end-to-end
- Parallel development possible (different slices)
- Natural for team-based migration

**Cons**:
- Cross-cutting concerns (sessions, config) must be established early
- Shared utilities need early extraction from functions.php
- Slices have dependencies (Articles need Feeds need Users)

### Variant D: Hybrid Entity-then-Graph

**Strategy**: Entity models first (1 pass), then follow call graph for business logic.

```
Phase 1 — Foundation:
  1a. SQLAlchemy models for ALL tables (entity dimension)
  1b. Config + environment setup
  1c. Flask/FastAPI app skeleton with routing

Phase 2 — Core Logic (call graph order):
  2a. Auth + Sessions (deepest dependency)
  2b. Preference system
  2c. Database utility functions (replace db_query/db_fetch)

Phase 3 — Business Logic (entity clusters):
  3a. Feed management (ttrss_feeds + ttrss_feed_categories)
  3b. Article management (ttrss_entries + ttrss_user_entries)
  3c. Feed update engine (rssfuncs → parser → storage)
  3d. Labels + Tags + Filters

Phase 4 — Handlers (frontend-backend contract):
  4a. RPC handler (state mutations)
  4b. Feeds handler (headline rendering)
  4c. Article handler
  4d. Preference handlers

Phase 5 — Cross-Cutting:
  5a. Plugin system
  5b. API (external)
  5c. Background worker (Celery)
  5d. Logging + Error handling

Phase 6 — Deployment:
  6a. Docker + CI/CD
  6b. Frontend adaptation
```

**Pros**:
- Models validated early against real schema
- Call graph guides implementation order (no missing deps)
- Entity clusters keep related code together
- Each phase is testable

**Cons**:
- More planning overhead
- Phase 1 is large (35 models)

### Variant E: Granular Multi-Pass

**Strategy**: Multiple fine-grained passes, each addressing one dimension.

```
Pass 1 — Models:     All SQLAlchemy models (entity dimension)
Pass 2 — Access:     Repository/service layer for each entity cluster
Pass 3 — Auth:       Authentication + authorization + sessions
Pass 4 — Config:     Configuration + environment + preferences
Pass 5 — Parsing:    Feed parser + item extractors (isolated, testable)
Pass 6 — Engine:     Feed update engine + caching + daemon
Pass 7 — Handlers:   All handler classes (one per iteration)
Pass 8 — API:        External REST API
Pass 9 — Plugins:    Plugin system + hook framework
Pass 10 — Frontend:  Adapt or rewrite frontend
Pass 11 — Deploy:    Docker + CI/CD + monitoring
```

**Pros**: Maximum granularity, each pass is small and focused
**Cons**: Many passes, slower overall, more integration testing needed

---

## Proposed Analysis Tools

### NetworkX + Leiden Community Detection

Use Python graph analysis to validate and refine the dimension analysis:

```python
import networkx as nx
from leidenalg import find_partition
import igraph

# Build call graph
G = nx.DiGraph()
# Add nodes: PHP files/functions
# Add edges: require/include/function calls
# Run Leiden community detection to find natural module boundaries

# Build entity graph
E = nx.Graph()
# Add nodes: database tables
# Add edges: foreign key relationships
# Run Leiden to find entity clusters

# Build coupling graph
C = nx.Graph()
# Add nodes: PHP classes
# Add edges: weighted by shared function calls / imports
# Run Leiden to find tightly coupled components
```

This can be automated by parsing the PHP source and building the graphs programmatically.

---

## Recommendation Matrix

| Criterion | Variant A | Variant B | Variant C | Variant D | Variant E |
|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|
| Time to first runnable code | Slow | Fast | Medium | Medium | Slow |
| Refactoring risk | Low | High | Medium | Low | Low |
| Testability per phase | Medium | Low | High | High | High |
| Parallel development | Low | Low | High | Medium | Medium |
| Dependency management | Easy | Hard | Medium | Easy | Easy |
| Planning overhead | Low | Low | Medium | Medium | High |
| Best for solo dev | Good | OK | Harder | **Best** | OK |
| Best for team | OK | Harder | **Best** | Good | Good |

### Initial Recommendation: **Variant D (Hybrid Entity-then-Graph)**

Rationale:
1. Models-first gives a solid, validated foundation
2. Call-graph ordering prevents "missing dependency" issues
3. Entity clusters keep related business logic together
4. Each phase is independently testable
5. Matches the project's solo/small-team nature

**To be discussed and finalized before migration starts.**

---

2. **Set up Python project skeleton** in `target-repos/`
3. **Build automated call graph** using NetworkX from PHP source
4. **Validate entity clusters** against actual SQL query patterns
5. **Create per-phase migration tickets** based on chosen variant
6. **Establish testing strategy** (unit tests per phase, integration tests per slice)

# Architecture Decision Log (ADL)

This directory contains Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) for the TT-RSS PHP→Python migration project.

## Format

Each ADR follows the standard template:
- **Status**: `proposed` → `accepted` / `rejected` / `superseded`
- **Context**: Why this decision is needed
- **Decision**: What was decided
- **Consequences**: What follows from the decision

## Decision Index

| ADR | Title | Status | Priority |
|-----|-------|--------|----------|
| [ADR-001](adr-001-migration-flow-variant.md) | Migration Flow Variant | proposed | P0 — blocks all migration work |
| [ADR-002](adr-002-python-framework.md) | Python Web Framework | proposed | P0 — blocks project skeleton |
| [ADR-003](adr-003-database-engine.md) | Database Engine Choice | proposed | P0 — blocks model layer |
| [ADR-004](adr-004-frontend-strategy.md) | Frontend Migration Strategy | proposed | P1 — blocks UI work |
| [ADR-005](adr-005-call-graph-analysis.md) | Automated Call Graph Analysis | proposed | P1 — informs migration ordering |

## Decision Dependencies

```
ADR-001 (Flow Variant)
  ├── depends on: ADR-002, ADR-003 (framework + DB inform flow)
  └── blocks: all migration phases

ADR-002 (Framework) + ADR-003 (DB)
  └── block: ADR-001 final decision, project skeleton creation

ADR-004 (Frontend)
  └── blocks: Phase 4+ (handler migration)

ADR-005 (Call Graph)
  └── informs: ADR-001 (validates community detection)
```

# ADR-001: Migration Flow Variant

- **Status**: proposed
- **Date proposed**: 2026-04-03
- **Deciders**: TBD
- **Depends on**: ADR-002, ADR-003

## Context

The PHP→Python migration requires a structured approach for ordering work across ~18,600 lines of application PHP code, 35 database tables, and 11 JavaScript files. Five flow variants were analyzed in `specs/09-migration-dimensions.md`, each driving migration by a different dimension.

The choice of variant determines:
- What gets built first
- When we get first runnable code
- How much refactoring risk we carry
- Whether work can be parallelized

## Options

### A: Entity-First (Bottom-Up)
Models first → DB access → utilities → handlers → plugins → frontend → deploy.
*Good foundation but slow to first runnable code.*

### B: Call-Graph-First (Top-Down)
Entry points → routing → handlers (with stubs) → DB layer → engine → polish.
*Fast skeleton but high refactoring risk when stubs replaced.*

### C: Vertical Slice (Feature-First)
Auth slice → Feeds slice → Articles slice → etc. Each end-to-end.
*Great for teams but cross-cutting concerns need early extraction.*

### D: Hybrid Entity-then-Graph (Recommended)
Phase 1: All SQLAlchemy models + app skeleton.
Phase 2: Core logic in call-graph order (auth → prefs → utilities).
Phase 3: Business logic by entity cluster (feeds → articles → labels → filters).
Phase 4: Handlers preserving frontend contract.
Phase 5: Cross-cutting (plugins, API, worker).
Phase 6: Deployment.
*Balanced: solid foundation, natural ordering, each phase testable.*

### E: Granular Multi-Pass
11 fine-grained passes (models → access → auth → config → parsing → engine → handlers → API → plugins → frontend → deploy).
*Maximum granularity but high coordination overhead.*

## Preliminary Recommendation

**Variant D** — balances foundation quality, testability per phase, and pragmatic ordering for solo/small-team work.

## Decision

**TBD** — to be discussed and accepted before migration begins.

## Consequences

- Chosen variant determines the phase structure for all subsequent work
- Phase breakdown becomes the migration backlog
- Testing strategy aligns to phase boundaries
- If Variant D: Phase 1 (models) is large (~35 models) but parallelizable

```


**Tool Call: Write adl/adr\-002\-python\-framework.md**
Status: Completed

# ADR-002: Python Web Framework

- **Status**: proposed
- **Date proposed**: 2026-04-03
- **Deciders**: TBD

## Context

The PHP source uses a custom handler-based dispatch system (`backend.php` routes `?op=X&method=Y` to handler classes). The Python replacement needs:

- HTTP routing with handler/blueprint organization
- JSON response serialization
- Session management (database-backed)
- CSRF protection
- Template rendering (for server-generated HTML fragments)
- Background task support (feed update daemon)
- Plugin/extension system compatibility

## Options

### Flask + Extensions
- **Flask** (WSGI, sync) + Flask-SQLAlchemy + Flask-Login + Flask-WTF + Celery
- Lightweight, matches TT-RSS's simplicity
- Mature ecosystem, well-documented
- Jinja2 templates for HTML fragment rendering
- Blueprints map cleanly to handler classes

### FastAPI + SQLAlchemy
- **FastAPI** (ASGI, async) + SQLAlchemy 2.0 async + Celery/ARQ
- Modern, auto-generated OpenAPI docs
- Async feed fetching could be significantly faster
- Pydantic models for request/response validation
- Less mature for server-rendered HTML patterns

### Django
- **Django** (WSGI) — full-featured with ORM, admin, auth built-in
- Heavier than needed for this project
- Django ORM is different from SQLAlchemy (migration complexity)
- Built-in admin could replace Pref_Users/Pref_System handlers
- Good plugin system (Django apps)

## Trade-off Analysis

| Criterion | Flask | FastAPI | Django |
|-----------|-------|---------|--------|
| Matches source architecture | Best | Good | Over-engineered |
| Async feed fetching | No (needs gevent/celery) | Native | No (needs celery) |
| Server-rendered HTML | Jinja2 (excellent) | Jinja2 (possible) | Django templates |
| Learning curve | Low | Medium | Medium |
| API documentation | Manual/Swagger ext | Auto OpenAPI | DRF needed |
| Background tasks | Celery | Celery/ARQ | Celery |
| Session management | Flask-Login | Custom/Starlette | Built-in |
| Community/maturity | Very high | High | Very high |

## Preliminary Recommendation

**Flask** — closest architectural match, simplest migration path, proven ecosystem.

Consider **FastAPI** if async feed fetching performance is a priority.

## Decision

**TBD**

## Consequences

- Framework choice determines project skeleton structure
- Affects ORM choice (Flask is SQLAlchemy-native; Django has its own ORM)
- Affects async strategy (Flask = Celery; FastAPI = native async + Celery)
- Affects testing approach (pytest-flask vs pytest-asyncio vs Django test client)

```


**Tool Call: Write adl/adr\-003\-database\-engine.md**
Status: Completed

Diff: /Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/adl/adr-003-database-engine.md
```
# ADR-003: Database Engine Choice

- **Status**: proposed
- **Date proposed**: 2026-04-03
- **Deciders**: TBD

## Context

The PHP source supports both MySQL and PostgreSQL via an adapter pattern. The Docker setup uses MariaDB 10.3 for development and MySQL 5.5 for production. Schema files exist in parallel for both engines (246 SQL files total).

Moving to Python with SQLAlchemy, we can:
1. Keep dual-database support (SQLAlchemy abstracts differences)
2. Choose one engine and simplify
3. Migrate to a different engine entirely

## Options

### A: Keep MySQL/MariaDB Only
- Zero data migration needed
- Docker setup already works
- MariaDB 10.3+ is solid
- Some features (JSON columns, window functions) are limited in older versions

### B: Migrate to PostgreSQL Only
- TT-RSS upstream historically preferred PostgreSQL
- Superior full-text search (replaces Sphinx dependency)
- Better JSON support, CTEs, window functions
- Better concurrent write performance
- Requires one-time data migration

### C: Keep Dual Support via SQLAlchemy
- SQLAlchemy dialect system handles differences
- Alembic can generate migrations for both
- More testing surface
- Some queries may need dialect-specific branches

## Trade-off Analysis

| Criterion | MySQL/MariaDB | PostgreSQL | Dual |
|-----------|--------------|------------|------|
| Migration effort | None | One-time schema + data | None |
| Full-text search | Needs Sphinx | Built-in (tsvector) | Complex |
| JSON support | Basic (5.7+) | Excellent (JSONB) | Lowest common |
| Operational familiarity | Current setup | May need new skills | Both |
| SQLAlchemy support | Excellent | Excellent | Excellent |
| Testing burden | 1x | 1x | 2x |
| Future flexibility | Good | Best | Best but costly |

## Preliminary Recommendation

**Option B: PostgreSQL** — simplifies the codebase, eliminates Sphinx dependency via native full-text search, and aligns with upstream TT-RSS preference. One-time migration cost is acceptable.

If team is MySQL-only: **Option A** is fine — SQLAlchemy makes the PHP adapter pattern unnecessary regardless.

## Decision

**TBD**

## Consequences

- If PostgreSQL: need data migration script (schema exists in source)
- If MySQL: keep existing Docker setup, add SQLAlchemy MySQL dialect
- If dual: double the migration testing, some queries need dialect handling
- Choice affects full-text search strategy (Sphinx vs PostgreSQL tsvector vs ElasticSearch)

```


**Tool Call: Write adl/adr\-004\-frontend\-strategy.md**
Status: Completed

Diff: /Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/adl/adr-004-frontend-strategy.md
```
# ADR-004: Frontend Migration Strategy

- **Status**: proposed
- **Date proposed**: 2026-04-03
- **Deciders**: TBD

## Context

The TT-RSS frontend is a server-rendered SPA hybrid using:
- **Prototype.js** (~1.7) — DOM manipulation, AJAX
- **Dojo Toolkit** (~1.8) — dijit widgets, data stores, tree components
- **Custom JS** — 11 application files (~3000 lines)
- **Server-rendered HTML** — headlines, dialogs, toolbars generated in PHP

Both Prototype.js and Dojo are legacy libraries (Prototype essentially unmaintained since 2015, Dojo 1.x superseded by Dojo 2+).

The frontend communicates with the backend through a well-defined JSON RPC contract via `backend.php?op=X&method=Y`.

## Options

### A: Keep Existing Frontend (Phase 1 only)
- Build Python backend with identical JSON API contract
- Frontend JS stays unchanged — served as static files
- Verify behavior parity by running same frontend against new backend
- Defer frontend modernization to Phase 2

### B: Rewrite with htmx (Server-Rendered)
- Closest to current architecture (server sends HTML fragments)
- Replace Prototype.js AJAX with htmx attributes
- Replace dijit widgets with lightweight alternatives (Alpine.js, vanilla JS)
- Incremental: can replace one component at a time

### C: Rewrite with React/Vue SPA
- Modern SPA with API-first backend
- Complete frontend rewrite
- Backend becomes pure REST/GraphQL API
- Highest effort, highest long-term maintainability

### D: Rewrite with Jinja2 + HTMX + Alpine.js
- Server-rendered pages with Jinja2 templates
- HTMX for AJAX interactions (partial page updates)
- Alpine.js for client-side interactivity (dropdowns, toggles)
- No heavy JS framework, keeps server-rendering pattern

## Trade-off Analysis

| Criterion | A: Keep | B: htmx | C: React/Vue | D: Jinja2+htmx+Alpine |
|-----------|---------|---------|--------------|----------------------|
| Migration effort | Minimal | Medium | Very high | Medium |
| Behavior parity verification | Easy | Medium | Hard | Medium |
| Can start immediately | Yes | No (needs backend first) | No | No |
| Long-term maintainability | Poor (legacy libs) | Good | Best | Good |
| Performance | Same | Better | Better | Better |
| Team skill requirements | None | Low | High (React/Vue) | Low |

## Preliminary Recommendation

**Option A for Phase 1** — keep existing frontend to validate backend migration with zero frontend risk.

**Option D for Phase 2** — Jinja2 + htmx + Alpine.js modernizes the frontend while preserving the server-rendered architecture that TT-RSS already uses.

## Decision

**TBD**

## Consequences

- If Option A: must preserve exact JSON response format from `backend.php`
- If Option A: must serve static JS/CSS files from Python app
- If Option D (Phase 2): need to map dijit widgets to Alpine.js equivalents
- Frontend choice doesn't block backend migration (decoupled by JSON contract)

```


**Tool Call: Write adl/adr\-005\-call\-graph\-analysis.md**

# ADR-005: Automated Call Graph Analysis

- **Status**: proposed
- **Date proposed**: 2026-04-03
- **Deciders**: TBD

## Context

The migration dimensions analysis (`specs/09-migration-dimensions.md`) identified 6 analysis dimensions and proposed using NetworkX + Leiden community detection to validate and refine the manually-identified module boundaries.

This ADR decides whether to invest in building automated source code analysis tooling before starting migration, or proceed with the manual analysis already completed.

## Options

### A: Build Automated Analysis (NetworkX + Leiden)

Build Python scripts that:
1. Parse PHP source for `require`/`include`/`new`/`extends`/`implements`/function calls
2. Build directed call graph in NetworkX
3. Build entity graph from table references in SQL queries
4. Run Leiden community detection on both graphs
5. Compare detected communities with manual clusters from specs
6. Generate visual dependency diagrams

**Effort**: ~1-2 days
**Tools**: NetworkX, python-igraph, leidenalg, matplotlib/graphviz

### B: Proceed with Manual Analysis

The manual analysis in specs already identifies:
- 8 call graph communities
- 10 entity clusters
- 6 frontend-backend coupling levels
- Complexity hotspot ranking

Proceed directly to migration using these as guide.

### C: Lightweight Static Analysis Only

Use existing PHP static analysis tools:
- `phpstan` or `psalm` for type inference
- `dephpend` for dependency graphs
- Generate visual output without custom scripting

## Trade-off Analysis

| Criterion | A: Full NetworkX | B: Manual only | C: Lightweight PHP tools |
|-----------|-----------------|----------------|-------------------------|
| Accuracy | High (quantitative) | Medium (expert judgment) | Medium |
| Effort | 1-2 days | 0 | 0.5 days |
| Reusability | High (scripts reusable for validation) | None | Low |
| Visualization | Excellent | None | Good |
| Leiden clustering | Yes | No | No |
| Validates manual analysis | Yes | N/A | Partially |

## Preliminary Recommendation

**Option A** if time permits — the investment is small (1-2 days) and the quantitative validation of migration ordering could prevent costly mistakes. The scripts are also reusable for tracking migration progress (e.g., "which communities are fully migrated?").

**Option B** if time is tight — the manual analysis is solid enough to start.

## Decision

**TBD**

## Consequences

- If Option A: creates a reusable toolset for migration progress tracking
- If Option A: may reveal unexpected dependency clusters not caught manually
- If Option B: risk of discovering hidden dependencies mid-migration
- If Option C: partial validation without custom investment

```

# 10 — MGPC Breakdown (Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints)

## Phase 0: Bottom-Up Requirements Saturation

### CoK Triple Expansion

**L5 — Topics** (explicit and implied):
```
Explicit:  PHP-to-Python migration, TT-RSS, RSS aggregator, behavioral preservation
Implied:   web framework selection, ORM mapping, feed parsing, authentication,
           plugin architecture, background processing, database migration,
           deployment modernization, security hardening, API compatibility,
           frontend adaptation, i18n preservation, testing strategy
```

**L4 — Areas** (solution patterns):
```
(PHP migration, belongs_to, language_migration)
(language_migration, has_pattern, {strangler_fig, big_bang, parallel_run, incremental_rewrite})
(RSS aggregator, belongs_to, content_aggregation)
(content_aggregation, has_pattern, {feed_polling, push_notification, pub_sub})
(behavioral_preservation, belongs_to, system_equivalence)
(system_equivalence, has_pattern, {contract_testing, shadow_traffic, regression_suite})
```

**L3 — Fields** (delivery mechanisms):
```
(language_migration, implements_via, {web_frameworks, ORMs, task_queues, containerization})
(content_aggregation, implements_via, {HTTP_clients, XML_parsers, scheduling_engines})
(system_equivalence, implements_via, {integration_tests, API_contract_tests, diff_testing})
```

**L2 — Disciplines** (cross-cutting concerns):
```
(web_frameworks, grounded_in, software_engineering)
(software_engineering, mandates, {security, testing, observability, documentation})
(ORMs, grounded_in, data_engineering)
(data_engineering, mandates, {schema_integrity, migration_safety, backup_strategy})
(containerization, grounded_in, devops)
(devops, mandates, {CI_CD, reproducibility, environment_parity})
```

**L1 — Domains**:
```
(software_engineering, part_of, technology) ✓
(data_engineering, part_of, technology) ✓
(devops, part_of, technology) ✓
Disjoint from: arts, humanities, natural_sciences ✓
```

### Saturation Output

```
L5 → {PHP migration, Python, TT-RSS, RSS, feed parsing, auth, plugins, daemon,
       DB migration, deploy, security, API, frontend, i18n, testing}
L4 → [language_migration]+{strangler_fig, incremental_rewrite}
      [content_aggregation]+{feed_polling, pub_sub}
      [system_equivalence]+{contract_testing, regression_suite}
L3 → [web_frameworks]+{Flask, FastAPI, Django}
      [ORMs]+{SQLAlchemy, Alembic}
      [task_queues]+{Celery, asyncio}
      [containerization]+{Docker, docker-compose}
L2 → [software_engineering]+{security, testing, observability}
      [data_engineering]+{schema_integrity, migration_safety}
      [devops]+{CI_CD, reproducibility}
L1 → [technology] ✓

Requirements:
  L4: behavioral preservation via contract testing, incremental migration strategy
  L3: framework + ORM + task queue + container decisions
  L2: security hardening mandatory, CI/CD mandatory, testing mandatory
Solution Space: {Flask+SQLAlchemy+Celery, FastAPI+SQLAlchemy+ARQ, Django+DjangoORM+Celery}
```

---

## Phase 1: Top-Down Intent Inference

### "Why?" Recursion (W-Functor)

```
"Migrate TT-RSS from PHP to Python"
→ why? "To modernize the technology stack"
→ why? "To improve maintainability, security, and developer productivity"
→ why? "To ensure long-term viability and reduce operational risk"
→ why? "To deliver reliable, secure software that serves its users"
→ why? "Reliable, secure software is intrinsically valuable"
         ← tautology = Mission
```

---

## MGPC Specification

### M — Mission

**Deliver a reliable, secure, and maintainable RSS aggregation platform by migrating TT-RSS from PHP to Python, preserving all functional behavior while improving the technology foundation.**

The mission is NOT "rewrite in Python" (that's a goal). The mission is the terminal value: reliable, secure, maintainable software that serves users. Python is the vehicle, not the destination.

### G — Goals

| ID | Goal | Litmus Test (changing it changes solution type) |
|----|------|------------------------------------------------|
| G1 | **Complete functional migration** — all TT-RSS features work identically in Python | If removed → no migration needed |
| G2 | **Preserve API contract** — existing REST API and frontend-backend JSON contract unchanged | If removed → can break clients, different project |
| G3 | **Preserve database schema** — existing data remains accessible without data migration (or with automated migration) | If removed → greenfield rewrite, not migration |
| G4 | **Modernize security** — fix known vulnerabilities (SHA1, no prepared statements, SSL, etc.) | If removed → just a port, not an improvement |
| G5 | **Containerized deployment** — Docker-based, CI/CD-ready | If removed → manual deployment, different ops model |
| G6 | **Plugin system parity** — plugin architecture preserved with equivalent hook system | If removed → no extensibility, different product |

### P — Premises (assumptions that must hold)

| ID | Premise | If false → consequence |
|----|---------|----------------------|
| P1 | **Python ecosystem has adequate RSS parsing libraries** (feedparser, lxml) | Goal G1 impossible — need custom parser |
| P2 | **SQLAlchemy can model the existing 35-table schema** | Goal G3 impossible — need different ORM or raw SQL |
| P3 | **Existing frontend JS can work with any backend that returns identical JSON** | Goal G2 impossible — frontend tightly coupled to PHP |
| P4 | **Team has Python web development competence** | All goals delayed — need training first |
| P5 | **Source code is complete and representative** (no hidden dependencies outside repo) | Goal G1 at risk — missing behavior |
| P6 | **The application's transactional script pattern can be preserved or improved in Python** | Goal G1 requires significant redesign |
| P7 | **Background feed updates can be handled by Celery or equivalent** | Goal G1 (daemon) at risk |
| P8 | **Existing .po/.mo locale files are compatible with Python gettext** | i18n breaks — need conversion |

### C — Constraints

#### Hard Constraints (violation = rejection)

| ID | Constraint | Source |
|----|-----------|--------|
| C1 | **Never modify source-repos/** — read-only reference | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |
| C2 | **All migrated code in target-repos/** | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |
| C3 | **Behavioral parity** — same input → same output for all endpoints | Migration definition |
| C4 | **Database compatibility** — must work with existing data (or provide automated migration) | Data preservation requirement |
| C5 | **No secrets in repo** — config via environment variables | Security best practice |
| C6 | **Spec traceability** — every migration phase references specs/ documents | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |

#### Soft Constraints (violation = penalty, not rejection)

| ID | Constraint | Penalty if violated |
|----|-----------|-------------------|
| C7 | **Prefer single database engine** (not dual MySQL+PostgreSQL) | Extra testing, complexity |
| C8 | **Prefer established libraries** over custom implementations | Maintenance burden |
| C9 | **Preserve plugin hook IDs and names** for documentation continuity | Minor confusion |
| C10 | **Keep deployment simple** (single docker-compose up) | Ops complexity |
| C11 | **Incremental migration** (avoid big-bang rewrite) | Risk of partial failure |
| C12 | **Test coverage ≥ 80%** for migrated code | Quality risk |

### Solution Space

From Phase 0 saturation:

```
Framework:  {Flask+SQLAlchemy+Celery, FastAPI+SQLAlchemy+ARQ, Django+DjangoORM+Celery}
Database:   {MySQL/MariaDB (keep), PostgreSQL (migrate), Dual (both)}
Frontend:   {Keep existing JS, htmx rewrite, React/Vue SPA, Jinja2+htmx+Alpine}
Migration:  {Entity-first, Call-graph-first, Vertical-slice, Hybrid, Granular}
Testing:    {pytest + contract tests, parallel-run validation, shadow traffic}
Deployment: {Docker + docker-compose, Kubernetes, bare metal}
```

Pending ADRs narrow this space: see `adl/` directory.

## Anti-Patterns to Avoid

| Anti-Pattern | Why Dangerous | Mitigation |
|-------------|---------------|------------|
| Big-bang rewrite | High risk of incomplete migration | Use incremental variant (ADR-001) |
| Gold-plating | Adding features during migration | Strict behavioral parity (C3) |
| Skipping Phase 0 models | Business logic has no foundation | Entity-first or hybrid variant |
| Ignoring security findings | Replicating known vulnerabilities | G4 explicitly requires fixes |
| Over-engineering plugin system | Python's module system is simpler | Keep hooks, simplify discovery |
| Dual-DB support "just in case" | Double testing burden | Decide in ADR-003 |
| Frontend rewrite during backend migration | Two moving targets | ADR-004 recommends Phase 1: keep JS |

---

## Research Findings: Spec-Kit Directory Structure Conventions

### 1. Is There a Standard "spec-kit" Format?

**Yes.** GitHub's official [spec-kit](https://github.com/github/spec-kit) (85K+ stars) defines a concrete standard via the `specify init` CLI. The generated structure is:

```
<project-root>/
├── .specify/
│   ├── memory/
│   │   └── constitution.md          # Governing principles (immutable)
│   ├── scripts/                     # Helper scripts (bash + powershell)
│   ├── templates/
│   │   ├── spec-template.md
│   │   ├── plan-template.md
│   │   ├── tasks-template.md
│   │   └── constitution-template.md
│   ├── specs/                       # Created per-feature
│   ├── extensions/
│   ├── presets/
│   └── init-options.json
├── .<agent-folder>/                 # e.g. .claude/commands/ or .github/agents/
│   └── speckit.*.md                 # Slash commands
└── .vscode/settings.json
```

Per-feature specs live in subdirectories:

```
specs/NNN-feature-name/
├── spec.md          # Feature specification (from /speckit.specify)
├── plan.md          # Implementation plan (from /speckit.plan)
├── research.md      # Technical research findings
├── data-model.md    # Data schemas
├── contracts/       # API and interface contracts
├── quickstart.md    # Key validation scenarios
└── tasks.md         # Executable task list (from /speckit.tasks)
```

**Key insight:** Spec-kit uses a **per-feature subdirectory model** under `specs/`, not a flat file approach. The `constitution.md` (project-level principles) lives in `.specify/memory/`, separate from feature specs.

### 2. ADR Placement: Inside specs/ or as a Sibling?

**The strong consensus across all standards is: ADRs should be a sibling directory, NOT inside specs/.**

| Standard/Tool | Default ADR Path | Source |
|---|---|---|
| [adr-tools](https://github.com/npryce/adr-tools) (5.4K stars) | `doc/adr/` | Nygard's original convention |
| [MADR](https://github.com/adr/madr) (2.1K stars) | `docs/decisions/` | adr.github.io recommendation |
| [Backstage](https://backstage.io/docs/architecture-decisions/) | `docs/architecture-decisions/` | Spotify's pattern |
| [arc42](https://arc42.org/overview) | Section 9 (own section, not nested in requirements) | Starke & Hruschka |
| [AWS Prescriptive Guidance](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/prescriptive-guidance/latest/architectural-decision-records/adr-process.html) | Dedicated ADR folder in documentation | AWS |
| [Martin Fowler](https://martinfowler.com/bliki/ArchitectureDecisionRecord.html) | `doc/adr/` or `docs/adr/` | Industry standard reference |
| [Microsoft Azure WAF](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/well-architected/architect-role/architecture-decision-record) | Standalone decision log | Microsoft |

**Rationale:** ADRs are a cross-cutting decision log that spans multiple features and concerns. Nesting them inside `specs/` would imply they belong to a single feature. ADRs reference and are referenced by specs, but they are a distinct artifact type with their own lifecycle (Proposed -> Accepted -> Deprecated -> Superseded).

**Recommendation:** ADRs as a sibling to `specs/`. Common names: `docs/decisions/`, `doc/adr/`, or `adl/` (Architecture Decision Log, as your project already uses).

### 3. Where Does a Mission/Requirements Document (MGPC) Go?

There is no single industry standard for this, but three clear patterns emerge:

**Pattern A -- Arc42 style (top-level section):** Arc42 places Introduction & Goals (Section 1) and Constraints (Section 2) as the very first documents, at the top level of the documentation hierarchy. Mission, goals, premises, and constraints are the foundational context that everything else derives from.

**Pattern B -- Spec-kit style (constitution):** Spec-kit puts the equivalent document (`constitution.md`) in `.specify/memory/` -- a dedicated "memory" directory that is project-wide and immutable. It is explicitly NOT inside `specs/` because it governs all specs.

**Pattern C -- Root-level file:** Many projects place their mission/charter as a top-level file (like `AGENTS.md`, `VISION.md`, or `PROJECT.md`) since it is the first thing a contributor should read.

**Recommendation:** A mission/requirements document like MGPC should live either:
- As a **top-level file** in `specs/` (e.g., `specs/00-mgpc.md` or `specs/00-mission.md`) if specs/ is the single source of truth for "what we're building and why", OR
- As a **dedicated top-level document** (e.g., `MGPC.md` or inside `.specify/memory/`) if you want to emphasize its constitutional/governing nature separate from feature specs.

The numbered-prefix approach (`00-`, `01-`, etc.) that your project already uses is a well-established pattern that puts the MGPC document first in sort order, signaling its primacy.

### 4. Common Patterns for Organizing Specs + ADRs + Requirements in One Workspace

Based on the research, here is the **composite best-practice structure** drawing from spec-kit, arc42, MADR, and adr-tools:

```
project-root/
├── AGENTS.md                        # Project rules & conventions (top-level entry point)
│
├── specs/                           # Specifications (the "what" and "why")
│   ├── 00-mission.md               # MGPC / Mission / Constitution (arc42 Section 1+2)
│   ├── 01-architecture.md          # System overview (arc42 Section 3+4+5)
│   ├── 02-database.md              # Domain-specific specs
│   ├── ...
│   └── NNN-feature-name/           # Per-feature specs (spec-kit pattern)
│       ├── spec.md
│       ├── plan.md
│       └── tasks.md
│
├── docs/decisions/                  # ADRs (MADR convention)
│   ├── README.md                   # Decision index + dependency graph
│   ├── 0001-choose-framework.md
│   ├── 0002-database-engine.md
│   └── ...
│
└── .specify/                        # Spec-kit tooling (if using spec-kit CLI)
    ├── memory/constitution.md
    └── templates/
```

### 5. Concrete Recommendations for Your Project

Your current structure (`specs/` + `adl/`) is already well-aligned with industry conventions. Specific observations:

**What you're doing right:**
- ADRs as a sibling to `specs/` (matches all major standards)
- Numbered prefixes for ordering (`00-`, `01-`, `adr-001-`)
- `README.md` in `adl/` as a decision index
- MGPC as a numbered file inside `specs/` (`10-mgpc-breakdown.md`)

**Minor refinements to consider:**
- The directory name `adl/` is non-standard. The most widely recognized paths are `docs/decisions/` (MADR), `doc/adr/` (adr-tools), or `docs/architecture-decisions/` (Backstage). If external contributors or tooling compatibility matters, `docs/decisions/` or `doc/adr/` would be more immediately recognizable.
- The MGPC document at `specs/10-mgpc-breakdown.md` sorts last among your specs. If it is foundational (mission/goals/constraints), placing it at `specs/00-mgpc.md` (before architecture) would better reflect its primacy per arc42's "Section 1 first" principle. Alternatively, some teams keep it as a standalone file at the root.
- ADR file numbering: your `adr-001-` prefix is compatible with both adr-tools (`NNNN-*`) and MADR (`nnnn-*`) conventions. Using 4-digit padding (`0001-`) would better match both standards.

**Bottom line:** There is no single canonical "spec-kit format" in the same way arc42 has 12 fixed sections. However, GitHub's spec-kit establishes the strongest emerging convention: `specs/` for feature specifications, a separate location for ADRs, and a "constitution" or mission document that sits above individual feature specs. Your project's structure is sound.

     1→# Architecture Decision Log (ADL)

     3→This directory contains Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) for the TT-RSS PHP→Python migration project.

     6→

```
# Architecture Decision Log

This directory contains Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) following [MADR](https://adr.github.io/madr/) conventions.

## Format

Each ADR follows the standard template:
- **Status**: `proposed` → `accepted` / `rejected` / `superseded`
- **Context**: Why this decision is needed
- **Decision**: What was decided
- **Consequences**: What follows from the decision

## Decision Index

| ADR | Title | Status | Priority |
|-----|-------|--------|----------|
| [0001](0001-migration-flow-variant.md) | Migration Flow Variant | proposed | P0 — blocks all migration work |
| [0002](0002-python-framework.md) | Python Web Framework | proposed | P0 — blocks project skeleton |
| [0003](0003-database-engine.md) | Database Engine Choice | proposed | P0 — blocks model layer |
| [0004](0004-frontend-strategy.md) | Frontend Migration Strategy | proposed | P1 — blocks UI work |
| [0005](0005-call-graph-analysis.md) | Automated Call Graph Analysis | proposed | P1 — informs migration ordering |

## Decision Dependencies

```
0001 (Flow Variant)
  ├── depends on: 0002, 0003 (framework + DB inform flow)
  └── blocks: all migration phases

0002 (Framework) + 0003 (DB)
  └── block: 0001 final decision, project skeleton creation

0004 (Frontend)
  └── blocks: Phase 4+ (handler migration)

0005 (Call Graph)
  └── informs: 0001 (validates community detection)
```

```

   202→
   203→## Anti-Patterns to Avoid
   204→
   205→| Anti-Pattern | Why Dangerous | Mitigation |
   206→|-------------|---------------|------------|
   207→| Big-bang rewrite | High risk of incomplete migration | Use incremental variant (ADR-001) |
   208→| Gold-plating | Adding features during migration | Strict behavioral parity (C3) |
   209→| Skipping Phase 0 models | Business logic has no foundation | Entity-first or hybrid variant |
   210→| Ignoring security findings | Replicating known vulnerabilities | G4 explicitly requires fixes |
   211→| Over-engineering plugin system | Python's module system is simpler | Keep hooks, simplify discovery |
   212→| Dual-DB support "just in case" | Double testing burden | Decide in ADR-003 |
   213→| Frontend rewrite during backend migration | Two moving targets | ADR-004 recommends Phase 1: keep JS |

    31→│   └── adr-005-call-graph-analysis.md
    32→├── memory/                ← Project memory (cross-session context)

    34→├── source-repos/          ← READ-ONLY: PHP source (ttrss-php/)
    35→│   └── ttrss-php/
    36→└── target-repos/          ← Python migration target (grows here)
    37→```
    38→
    39→## Critical Rules
    40→
    41→### Storage Rules
    42→1. **NEVER** write files into `~/.claude/projects/*/memory/` — all memory goes to `./memory/`
    43→2. **NEVER** modify anything inside `source-repos/` — it is read-only reference
    44→3. **NEVER** store project specs, memory, or rules in `.claude/` — that dir is only for Claude-specific config (settings, skills)
    45→4. All specs, memory, rules, and artifacts go in the **project root** under their respective directories
    46→5. This ensures cross-platform portability (not tied to Claude's home directory)
    47→
    48→### Migration Rules
    49→6. Target Python code goes into `target-repos/` — this is where the migrated project grows
    50→7. Every spec document in `specs/` must cross-reference source files by relative path (e.g., `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/db.php`) rather than duplicating source code
    51→8. Specs may include **reasonable code examples** to highlight important architectural decisions, but must not be a copy of the source
    52→9. When migrating, always verify behavior parity against the source spec before marking a component complete
    53→
    54→### Analysis Rules
    55→10. Use deep web research for any complicated architectural topic (PHP patterns, 3-tier architecture, ORM vs transactional script, etc.)
    56→11. For source code analysis dimensions (call graph, entity graph, etc.), consider using NetworkX and Leiden community detection
    57→12. Migration flow is driven by dimensions documented in `specs/09-migration-dimensions.md` — discuss and choose flow before starting migration
    58→
    59→### Quality Rules
    60→13. Preserve all functional behavior from the PHP source

## Assistant

Clean. Here's what changed and why:

## Changes Made

### 1. `adl/` → `docs/decisions/` (MADR convention)
- **Why**: `adl/` is non-standard. [MADR](https://adr.github.io/madr/), adr-tools, Backstage, and arc42 all use `docs/decisions/` or `doc/adr/`. Went with MADR as the most widely adopted.
- **Numbering**: `adr-001-` → `0001-` (4-digit padding per MADR/adr-tools standard)

### 2. MGPC moved to `specs/00-mgpc.md` (was `specs/10-`)
- **Why**: MGPC is foundational — it governs all other specs (Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints). Arc42 places "Introduction & Goals" as Section 1 (before architecture). GitHub spec-kit puts the equivalent (`constitution.md`) above specs entirely. Having it sort first (`00-`) reflects its primacy.
- **All other specs renumbered**: architecture is now `01-`, database `02-`, etc.
- **All internal cross-references updated** across all 11 spec files.

### 3. Final conformant structure
```
specs/                     ← Spec-kit (arc42-inspired ordering)
├── 00-mgpc.md             ← Constitution: Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints
├── 01-architecture.md     ← System overview (arc42 §3-5)
├── 02..10-*.md            ← Domain-specific specs
docs/decisions/            ← ADRs (MADR convention, sibling to specs/)
├── README.md              ← Decision index
└── 0001..0005-*.md        ← Individual decisions
```

This follows industry conventions: ADRs are a **sibling** to specs (not nested), and the mission/requirements document is the **first** spec in sort order.

## User

Cool. But is MGPC - is standard abbrev? Migh also need rename to 00-mission, etc& deep reseach it.

**Tool Call: Research MGPC naming conventions**
Status: Completed

I now have comprehensive data. Here is the full analysis.

---

# Research Report: Is "MGPC" a Standard Abbreviation?

## 1. MGPC Is NOT a Standard or Recognized Abbreviation

**Conclusive finding: "MGPC" (Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints) is not used anywhere outside this project.** A web search for `"MGPC" "mission goals premises constraints"` returned zero results. The acronym does not appear in:

- Any software engineering textbook or standard
- Any requirements engineering framework (IEEE, ISO, IREB)
- Any project management body of knowledge (PMBOK, PRINCE2, SAFe)
- Any architecture documentation standard (arc42, C4, TOGAF, RUP)
- Any open-source project templates (spec-kit, ADR templates)

The term appears to be a project-local invention in this repository's `specs/00-mgpc.md` and `AGENTS.md`.

## 2. What Standard Frameworks Call This Document

Here is how every major framework names the document that captures mission/vision, goals, assumptions, and constraints:

| Framework | Document Name | Covers Mission? | Covers Goals? | Covers Assumptions? | Covers Constraints? |
|-----------|--------------|:-:|:-:|:-:|:-:|
| **PMBOK (PMI)** | **Project Charter** | Yes (purpose/justification) | Yes (objectives, success criteria) | Yes (assumptions) | Yes (constraints) |
| **arc42** | **Introduction and Goals** (Section 1) | Partial (requirements overview) | Yes (quality goals) | No (separate) | Yes (in Section 2) |
| **RUP** | **Vision Document** | Yes (problem statement, positioning) | Yes (stakeholder needs, features) | Yes (assumptions) | Yes (constraints) |
| **TOGAF** | **Architecture Vision** / **Statement of Architecture Work** | Yes (business context) | Yes (architecture objectives) | Yes (assumptions) | Yes (constraints) |
| **SAFe** | **Vision** + **Solution Intent** | Yes (vision) | Yes (features, capabilities) | Implicit | Implicit |
| **IEEE 830 / ISO 29148** | **Software Requirements Specification** (SRS) | Partial (purpose, scope) | Yes (requirements) | Yes (assumptions) | Yes (constraints) |
| **Agile / Lean** | **Product Vision** or **Project Charter** | Yes | Yes | Sometimes | Sometimes |
| **GitHub spec-kit** | **constitution.md** | No (principles, not mission) | No (governance, not goals) | No | No (enforcement, not constraints) |
| **PRINCE2** | **Project Brief** / **Project Initiation Document** | Yes | Yes | Yes | Yes |

## 3. What spec-kit's "constitution.md" Actually Is

Based on crawling the actual spec-kit source, `constitution.md` is **not** analogous to your MGPC document. It is a governance and architectural principles document containing:

- **Immutable development principles** (e.g., "Library-First", "Test-First Imperative", "CLI Interface Mandate")
- **Amendment procedures and versioning**
- **Compliance review expectations**

It does NOT contain mission, goals, assumptions, or constraints. It is more like an "Architecture Decision Principles" document. So `constitution.md` is **not** the right name for what your `00-mgpc.md` contains.

## 4. Analysis: Which Name Best Fits Mission + Goals + Premises + Constraints?

The content of your `00-mgpc.md` maps most closely to **two** well-known document types:

### Best Match: **Project Charter**
- The PMBOK Project Charter is the single most widely recognized document that contains ALL four elements: purpose/mission, objectives/goals, assumptions, and constraints.
- It is understood across industries, methodologies, and roles (PMs, architects, developers, stakeholders).
- It is THE standard artifact that formally authorizes a project and defines its boundaries.

### Second Best: **Vision Document** (RUP)
- The RUP Vision Document also covers all four elements, plus stakeholder analysis.
- Well-known in software engineering circles, less so outside them.
- The word "vision" is widely understood but slightly more abstract/aspirational than what your document contains.

### Why NOT the Other Options:

| Candidate Name | Rejection Reason |
|---|---|
| `00-mission.md` | Too narrow -- only describes one of the four sections (Mission) |
| `00-introduction-and-goals.md` | arc42-specific; does not cover assumptions/constraints; overly verbose filename |
| `00-requirements.md` | Too broad; implies detailed functional requirements, not foundational framing |
| `00-constitution.md` | spec-kit meaning is "governance principles", not mission/goals/constraints; also carries political/legal connotations that could confuse |
| `00-mgpc.md` | Unrecognizable to anyone outside this project |

## 5. Recommendation

**Rename `00-mgpc.md` to `00-project-charter.md`.**

Rationale:

1. **Maximum recognizability**: "Project Charter" is understood by every PM, BA, architect, and developer who has worked in any structured methodology (PMBOK, Agile, PRINCE2, SAFe, RUP). It is the single most universally recognized name for this type of document.

2. **Accurate scope**: A project charter canonically contains purpose/mission, objectives/goals, assumptions (your "premises"), and constraints -- exactly the four MGPC sections.

3. **Framework-neutral**: Unlike "Vision Document" (RUP-specific) or "Introduction and Goals" (arc42-specific), "Project Charter" is methodology-agnostic.

4. **Subtitle preserves detail**: The document's H1 heading can still read `# 00 -- Project Charter: Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints` to make the contents immediately clear without relying on an opaque acronym.

5. **"Premises" vs "Assumptions"**: Consider also renaming "Premises" to "Assumptions" in the document body, since every standard framework uses "assumptions" (PMBOK, IEEE, TOGAF). "Premises" is philosophically precise but not the industry term. If you prefer to keep "Premises" for its semantic precision (assumptions that MUST hold, not just things we hope are true), add a parenthetical: `### P -- Premises (Assumptions That Must Hold)`.

### Concrete Change

```
specs/00-mgpc.md  -->  specs/00-project-charter.md
```

Update heading:
```markdown
# 00 -- Project Charter: Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints
```

Update all references in `AGENTS.md` from `00-mgpc.md` / `MGPC` to `00-project-charter.md` / `Project Charter`.

- [IEEE Std 1233-1998: Guide for Developing System Requirements Specifications](https://ranger.uta.edu/~huber/cse4316/Docs/IEEEStd1233-1998.pdf)

## Assistant

Done. Summary of what changed and why:

## Research Result

**"MGPC" is not a recognized abbreviation** — it's a PE_Library-internal term with zero usage in industry literature.

**"Project Charter"** is the universally recognized name (PMBOK, Agile, PRINCE2, SAFe, RUP) for a document containing exactly these four elements:
- **Mission** → Purpose/Justification
- **Goals** → Objectives/Success Criteria
- **Premises** → Assumptions (that must hold)
- **Constraints** → Hard/soft boundaries

## Changes Applied

| Before | After | Rationale |
|--------|-------|-----------|
| `specs/00-mgpc.md` | `specs/00-project-charter.md` | Standard name per PMBOK/Agile/PRINCE2 |
| `# 00 — MGPC: Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints` | `# 00 — Project Charter` | Recognizable to any practitioner |
| `## MGPC Specification` (section heading) | `## Charter Specification (Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints)` | Self-documenting |

# Compliance Review: TT-RSS PHP-to-Python Migration Spec-Kit

## 1. FACTUAL ERRORS AND STRUCTURAL PROBLEMS

### 1.1 ADR-0001 cross-references the wrong spec file

**File**: `docs/decisions/0001-migration-flow-variant.md`, line 10

The ADR states: "Five flow variants were analyzed in `specs/09-migration-dimensions.md`". The migration dimensions document is `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`, not `09`. Spec `09` is the source code index. This error is also present in `docs/decisions/0005-call-graph-analysis.md`, line 9, which states the same incorrect path.

### 1.2 Incorrect MySQL migration file count

**File**: `specs/02-database.md`, line 16

States "124 MySQL migration scripts" for `schema/versions/mysql/`. The actual directory contains 122 files (verified via filesystem). The spec further claims `{3-124}.sql` implying a continuous range of 122, while the table text says 124. The PostgreSQL line says "122 PostgreSQL migration scripts" -- the MySQL count is inconsistent with itself.

### 1.3 Incorrect file size claims for feeds.php

**File**: `specs/09-source-index.md`, line 60 / `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`, line 131

Claims `classes/feeds.php` is "~38KB". The actual file is 38,165 bytes / 1,163 lines. The specs also say "38KB" in 10-migration-dimensions but elsewhere in 01-architecture (line 214) the same file is not listed with size. The "38KB" figure is correct in bytes but the line count (~1163) is never stated anywhere, while spec 09-source-index claims the entire "Handler classes" category is "~4,500 lines" across 10 files. With feeds.php at 1163, api.php at 792, and rpc.php at 654 that is already 2,609 lines from just 3 files -- the "~4,500" estimate appears low.

### 1.4 Incorrect line count for api.php and rpc.php

**File**: `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`, lines 131-132

Claims `classes/api.php` is "22KB" and `classes/rpc.php` is "15KB". Actual: api.php is 792 lines, rpc.php is 654 lines. These are ~22KB and ~15KB in bytes, but expressing PHP handler complexity in bytes rather than lines is misleading and inconsistent with the rest of the spec kit, which uses lines everywhere else.

### 1.5 SINGLE_USER_MODE line reference is wrong

**File**: `specs/06-security.md`, line 19

Claims SINGLE_USER_MODE auth bypass is at `functions.php:750-770`. The actual occurrences are at lines 708 and 831. Lines 750-770 do not contain SINGLE_USER_MODE.

### 1.6 Inconsistent source file path conventions

**Files**: `AGENTS.md` line 7 vs all spec files

AGENTS.md defines the project layout with source at `source-repos/ttrss-php/`. Multiple specs say "All paths relative to `source-repos/ttrss-php/`" but then list paths like `ttrss/classes/feeds.php`. The actual filesystem path is `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/feeds.php`. AGENTS.md rule 7 says to use relative paths like `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/db.php`, but no spec actually uses this full relative path format. Every spec omits the `source-repos/ttrss-php/` prefix and says "All paths relative to" -- this is inconsistent with the AGENTS.md directive.

### 1.7 rssfuncs.php line count discrepancy

**File**: `specs/01-architecture.md`, line 215

Claims `rssfuncs.php` is "~1300" lines. Actual: 1,431 lines. That is a 10% error.

### 1.8 Locale count inconsistency

**File**: `specs/08-deployment.md`, line 164

States "18+ locales" and lists 20 language codes in the text. The actual locale directory contains exactly 20 directories (ca_CA through zh_TW). The spec text lists only short codes like "ca, cs, de" rather than the actual directory names like "ca_CA, cs_CZ, de_DE". This is imprecise enough to cause a developer to look for the wrong directory names.

---

## 2. WHAT IS MISSING

### 2.1 No business rules documented anywhere

No spec documents the actual business logic rules. Examples of undocumented business rules:

- How article deduplication works (by GUID? by content hash? both?)
- How filter rules are evaluated (AND vs OR, evaluation order, match_any_rule flag semantics)
- How scoring works (score increment/decrement rules, range, display thresholds)
- How feed update intervals interact with user-level defaults and per-feed overrides
- How the "adaptive" view_mode works (what SQL does it generate?)
- How article purging/expiry works (per-feed vs global, count vs age)
- How the catchup operation works across feeds vs categories vs "all"
- How feed categories nest (max depth? what happens on circular reference?)
- What "orig_feed_id" in ttrss_user_entries means and when it gets populated
- How PubSubHubbub subscription lifecycle works

These are the rules a developer must replicate. They are not documented.

### 2.2 No complete function-level inventory of functions.php and functions2.php

**File**: `specs/01-architecture.md`, `specs/09-source-index.md`

These two files contain ~4,400 lines of core utility functions. The specs mention them as "kitchen sink" and "core utilities" but never enumerate the functions. A developer cannot migrate what is not specified. The spec must list every public function in functions.php and functions2.php with its signature and purpose, or at minimum group them by domain.

### 2.3 No PHP-to-Python mapping with concrete library choices

**Requirement 8**: "Include Python migration mapping (PHP pattern -> Python equivalent) with concrete library choices."

`specs/10-migration-dimensions.md` Dimension 6 has a high-level pattern table (line 140-153) but it is shallow. It maps `$_SESSION` to "Flask session / Django middleware" -- these are not equivalent. There is no mapping for:
- PHP's `serialize()`/`unserialize()` (used in plugin storage) -> Python `json` or `pickle`
- PHP's `mb_*` functions -> Python's native Unicode
- PHP's `DOMDocument` / `SimpleXML` -> Python `lxml.etree` / `xml.etree`
- PHP's `curl_*` -> Python `requests` or `httpx`
- PHP's `preg_*` flags (PCRE vs Python re differences)
- PHP's `gettext` runtime -> Python `gettext` module specifics
- PHP's `mcrypt` -> Python `cryptography` (Fernet? AES-GCM? key derivation?)
- PHP's `PHPMailer` -> Python `smtplib` + `email.mime`
- PHP's `pcntl_fork()` (daemon workers) -> Python `multiprocessing` or Celery
- PHP's `flock()` -> Python `fcntl.flock()` or Redis locks

### 2.4 No sequence diagrams

**Requirement 9**: "Have entity-relationship diagrams, data flow diagrams, sequence diagrams (text-based)."

The specs contain ER diagrams (02-database) and layer diagrams (01-architecture), but there are zero sequence diagrams. The request lifecycle in 01-architecture (lines 126-179) uses numbered step lists, not sequence diagrams. A sequence diagram for the feed update flow, the login flow, the article marking flow, and the headline loading flow would show inter-component interactions that the step lists do not capture (especially timing, parallelism, and error paths).

### 2.5 No data flow diagrams

There is no diagram showing how data flows through the system during key operations: feed fetch -> parse -> filter -> store -> cache update -> counter update. The caching spec (07) has a layered stack diagram but it is a static inventory, not a flow.

### 2.6 No error handling documentation

No spec documents the application's error handling strategy:
- What happens when a feed fetch fails? (retry? mark feed? error count?)
- What happens when article parsing fails? (skip article? skip feed?)
- What HTTP error codes does the application return and under what conditions?
- How does the `ttrss_error_log` table get populated? What triggers a log entry?
- What are the error codes in `errors.php`? (This file is listed in 09-source-index but never described.)

### 2.7 No testing strategy spec

**Requirement 1**: "Be comprehensive enough to drive actual migration work."

There is no spec for testing. The charter mentions "contract testing" and "regression suite" (00-project-charter, line 71-72) and constraint C12 sets an 80% coverage target, but there is no document that defines:
- What constitutes a test case for behavioral parity
- How to validate that Python output matches PHP output for each endpoint
- Which endpoints need contract tests
- How to set up test fixtures (what data in which tables)
- Whether to use golden-file testing, snapshot testing, or live comparison

### 2.8 No config.php-dist variable inventory

**File**: `specs/01-architecture.md`

Lists `config.php-dist` as "Config template" with "~200" lines but never enumerates the configuration constants. A developer cannot build a Python config system without knowing every config variable, its type, default value, and where it is used. The deployment spec (08) lists 6 environment variables from docker-entrypoint.sh but the actual config.php-dist contains 30+ constants (DB_TYPE, SELF_URL_PATH, FEED_CRYPT_KEY, SPHINX_SERVER, PUBSUBHUBBUB_HUB, PUBSUBHUBBUB_ENABLED, ENABLE_REGISTRATION, etc.).

### 2.9 No OPML import/export format specification

The specs mention OPML import/export in 03-api-routing and 09-source-index but never document the OPML format, the import logic (duplicate handling, category creation), or the export structure. This is a complete feature that must be replicated.

### 2.10 No email digest documentation

`digest.php` is listed in 09-source-index but the digest feature is never specified:
- When are digests sent? (scheduled? user preference?)
- What content is included?
- What templates are used? (the templates directory has 6 template files)
- What email configuration is required?

### 2.11 No registration flow documentation

`register.php` is listed as an entry point but the user registration flow is never described: what fields, what validation, is email verification required, what access_level is assigned, is CAPTCHA used.

### 2.12 No install wizard documentation

`ttrss/install/index.php` exists in the source but is not mentioned in any spec. A developer would not know whether to replicate this functionality.

### 2.13 Missing ADRs for significant decisions

**Requirement 5**: "Have complete ADR coverage for ALL significant decisions (not just 5 obvious ones)."

Five ADRs exist. The following significant decisions have no ADR:
- **ORM vs raw SQL** (the specs assume SQLAlchemy but this is a major architectural decision)
- **Session management strategy** (database-backed PHP sessions -> what in Python?)
- **Password hashing migration** (how to handle existing SHA1 hashes during transition)
- **Feed credential encryption** (mcrypt -> what algorithm, key migration)
- **Plugin system implementation** (pluggy vs stevedore vs custom -- the spec lists options but makes no decision)
- **Background worker architecture** (Celery vs asyncio vs APScheduler)
- **Logging strategy** (SQL logging vs Python logging vs structured logging)
- **i18n approach** (gettext compatibility, .po file handling)
- **Feed parsing library** (feedparser vs lxml vs custom, with ATOM/RSS compat)
- **SSRF protection strategy** (mentioned in security spec but no decision)
- **Rate limiting strategy** (mentioned in security checklist but no decision)
- **API versioning** (the spec mentions "API v2" consideration but no ADR)

### 2.14 No edge case documentation

**Requirement 10**: "Document ALL business rules, edge cases, and implicit behavior."

Zero edge cases are documented. Examples:
- What happens when a feed URL returns a redirect? (permanent vs temporary)
- What happens with feeds that require HTTP authentication?
- How does the system handle feeds with invalid XML?
- What happens when the database connection drops mid-transaction?
- How does the system handle concurrent mark-as-read operations?
- What is the behavior when a user deletes a feed that has shared articles?
- How does the system handle timezone differences in feed timestamps?
- What happens when plugin storage is corrupted (invalid serialized PHP)?

### 2.15 No search functionality specification

Feeds::search is listed in 03-api-routing but the search feature is never documented: what fields are searched, what operators are supported, how does Sphinx integration work, what happens when Sphinx is unavailable.

---

## 3. WHAT IS OVER-ENGINEERED

### 3.1 The CoK Triple Expansion in 00-project-charter is academic filler

**File**: `specs/00-project-charter.md`, lines 6-74

The "Phase 0: Bottom-Up Requirements Saturation" section with its "CoK Triple Expansion", "L5 Topics", "L4 Areas", "L3 Fields", "L2 Disciplines", "L1 Domains" taxonomy is a knowledge management framework that adds zero actionable information to the spec. The "Saturation Output" at line 55 just restates what is already obvious. The "W-Functor" recursion at line 82 is a philosophy exercise. A developer reading this to understand the migration will skip it entirely. It occupies 70+ lines that could contain actual requirements.

### 3.2 The "Anti-Patterns to Avoid" section is generic

**File**: `specs/00-project-charter.md`, lines 205-216

"Big-bang rewrite", "Gold-plating", "Over-engineering plugin system" -- these are general software engineering advice, not project-specific anti-patterns derived from source analysis. A project-specific anti-pattern would be: "Do not replicate the dual-iteration pattern in db_fetch_assoc loops; use SQLAlchemy result sets directly."

### 3.3 Variant E (Granular Multi-Pass) adds no value

**File**: `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`, lines 284-303

Variant E is just Variant D with more passes. It has 3 lines of pros/cons. It exists to pad the option count. The recommendation matrix already scores it as inferior to D on most criteria.

### 3.4 The Dimension 4 (Coupling/Cohesion) table is subjective labels with no data

**File**: `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`, lines 109-119

"LOW", "HIGH", "MEDIUM" assessments with no quantitative backing. This is the spec author's opinion, not analysis. The proposed call graph tooling (ADR-0005) would provide this data, but the spec presents opinions as if they are findings.

---

## 4. WHAT IS INAPPROPRIATE IN SCOPE

### 4.1 Specs describe WHAT but not HOW -- wrong level of detail for migration

Every "Python Migration Notes" section (present in specs 01-07) is a bullet list of suggestions rather than a migration specification. For example:

**File**: `specs/02-database.md`, lines 224-231

"Recommended: SQLAlchemy ORM with Alembic migrations" is a suggestion, not a spec. A spec would include: the SQLAlchemy model definition for at least the 3 most complex tables (ttrss_user_entries, ttrss_feeds, ttrss_filters2), the Alembic migration strategy for the 35 tables, and the data migration script outline.

**File**: `specs/05-plugin-system.md`, lines 213-223

Lists 4 possible libraries (pluggy, stevedore, custom, signals) without committing to any. A developer cannot migrate the plugin system from this information.

### 4.2 The source-index (spec 09) is an inventory, not a spec

**File**: `specs/09-source-index.md`

This is a file listing with "Purpose" and "Spec Refs" columns. It repeats information already in specs 01-08. It does not contain any information that is not derivable from the filesystem itself plus the other specs. A developer with access to the source and specs 01-08 gains nothing from this file.

### 4.3 Deployment spec focuses on the PHP stack instead of the Python target

**File**: `specs/08-deployment.md`

90% of this document describes the existing PHP Docker/Nginx/PHP-FPM setup. This is reference material, not a migration spec. The "Python Migration Notes" section (lines 188-205) is 18 lines -- a skeleton, not a deployment specification. The spec should specify the target Docker image structure, the gunicorn/uvicorn configuration, the Celery worker setup, the health check endpoints, and the CI/CD pipeline for the Python project.

### 4.4 Frontend spec over-documents legacy JS libraries that will not be migrated in Phase 1

**File**: `specs/04-frontend.md`

The Dijit Widgets table (lines 163-178), Custom Dojo Extensions table (lines 182-188), and CSS Files table (lines 154-162) are reference material for the existing frontend, which the preliminary recommendation (ADR-0004) says to keep unchanged in Phase 1. This is the wrong focus: the spec should document the backend-frontend contract (JSON shapes, HTML fragment structure) in detail, because that contract is what the Python backend must replicate. The actual JSON response payloads are shown for only 2 of the approximately 40+ endpoints.

### 4.5 All 5 ADRs are "proposed" with "TBD" decisions -- the spec-kit is unactionable

**Files**: All files in `docs/decisions/`

Every ADR has `Status: proposed` and `Decision: TBD`. ADRs 0001, 0002, and 0003 are labeled "P0 -- blocks all migration work / blocks project skeleton / blocks model layer". The spec-kit is therefore explicitly self-blocking. No migration work can begin. A spec-kit that prevents work from starting has failed its primary purpose.

### 4.6 The traceability matrix is too coarse to be useful

**File**: `specs/00-project-charter.md`, lines 186-201

Fourteen rows, all with status "Not started". This is a template, not a traceability matrix. A useful matrix would trace individual PHP functions/methods to their Python equivalents, with test case references.
