## COMPREHENSIVE BUSINESS RULES EXTRACTION FROM TTRSS-PHP

### 1. ARTICLE DEDUPLICATION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`

- **GUID Construction & Hashing** (lines 550-562):
  - Article GUID extracted from: article ID → feed link → title-based fallback
  - GUID prefixed with `owner_uid` for multi-user isolation: `$entry_guid = "$owner_uid,$entry_guid"`
  - GUID hashed with SHA1: `$entry_guid_hashed = db_escape_string('SHA1:' . sha1($entry_guid))`

- **Content Hash Storage** (lines 707, 727-750):
  - Content hash computed: `$content_hash = "SHA1:" . sha1($entry_content)`
  - Stored in `ttrss_entries.content_hash` on INSERT

- **Duplicate Detection Logic** (lines 711-766):
  - Check if entry exists by GUID: `SELECT id FROM ttrss_entries WHERE (guid = '$entry_guid' OR guid = '$entry_guid_hashed')`
  - If NOT found: Create new base entry (lines 720-750)
  - If found: Update `date_updated` to NOW() (lines 762-763) to prevent reversion on purge
  - Check for user-specific duplicate via `ALLOW_DUPLICATE_POSTS` preference (line 804):
    - If enabled: `dupcheck_qpart = "AND (feed_id = '$feed' OR feed_id IS NULL)"`
    - If disabled: `dupcheck_qpart = ""` (global dedup)

- **N-gram Title Similarity** (lines 867-882, PostgreSQL only):
  - Threshold defined by `_NGRAM_TITLE_DUPLICATE_THRESHOLD` constant
  - Query: `SELECT COUNT(*) AS similar FROM ttrss_entries, ttrss_user_entries WHERE similarity(title, '$entry_title') >= "._NGRAM_TITLE_DUPLICATE_THRESHOLD." AND owner_uid = $owner_uid`
  - If similar count > 0: Mark article as read (unread = 'false')

---

### 2. FILTER EVALUATION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions2.php`

- **Filter Loading** (functions2.php, lines 1491-1563):
  - Load from `ttrss_filters2` where `owner_uid = $owner_uid AND enabled = true`
  - Ordered by `order_id, title`
  - Rules loaded from `ttrss_filters2_rules` (with category inheritance via parent categories)
  - Actions loaded from `ttrss_filters2_actions`

- **Filter Matching Logic** (rssfuncs.php, lines 1272-1348):
  - **match_any_rule flag** (lines 1322-1332):
    - **TRUE (OR logic)**: Any rule matching causes overall filter match
    - **FALSE (AND logic)**: ALL rules must match
  - **Rule Types** (lines 1288-1318):
    - `title`: Regex match on article title (case-insensitive)
    - `content`: Regex match on article content (case-insensitive)
    - `both`: Regex match on title OR content
    - `link`: Regex match on article link
    - `author`: Regex match on article author
    - `tag`: Regex match against any tag

  - **Rule Inversion** (line 1320): `if ($rule_inverse) $match = !$match`
  - **Filter Inversion** (line 1335): `if ($inverse) $filter_match = !$filter_match`

- **Filter Actions** (lines 1338-1343):
  - Actions array: Each matched filter adds all its actions
  - **Special**: "stop" action (line 1342) terminates processing and returns immediately

- **Possible Action Types** (loaded from `ttrss_filter_actions` table):
  - `filter` (type): Skip/filter article
  - `catchup` (type): Mark as read
  - `mark` (type): Star/mark article
  - `publish` (type): Publish article
  - `score` (type): Modify score (numeric param)
  - `label` (type): Add label (param = label caption)
  - `tag` (type): Add tag (comma-separated params)
  - `stop` (type): Stop processing

---

### 3. ARTICLE SCORING

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`

- **Score Calculation** (lines 1370-1379):
  - Sum all "score" type filter actions: `$score += $f["param"]`
  - Returns integer value (range unbounded in code, visually represented via ranges)

- **Initial Score Determination** (line 828):
  - `$score = calculate_article_score($article_filters)`

- **Score-based Default Actions** (lines 845-863):
  - If score >= -500 AND no "catchup" filter: Mark as unread
  - If score < -500 OR "catchup" filter present: Mark as read
  - If "mark" filter OR score > 1000: Mark as starred
  - If "publish" filter: Mark as published

- **Score Display Ranges** (functions2.php, lines 1565-1577):
  - score > 100: "score_high.png"
  - 0 < score <= 100: "score_half_high.png"
  - -100 <= score < 0: "score_half_low.png"
  - score < -100: "score_low.png"
  - score = 0: "score_neutral.png"

### 4. FEED UPDATE INTERVALS

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`

- **Per-Feed vs User Default Logic** (lines 84-107):
  - If `ttrss_feeds.update_interval = 0`: Use user's `DEFAULT_UPDATE_INTERVAL` preference
  - If `ttrss_feeds.update_interval > 0`: Use feed-specific interval
  - User preference value of `-1` disables updates

- **Update Need Detection Query** (lines 84-107, PostgreSQL example):
  ```sql
  ((ttrss_feeds.update_interval = 0
    AND ttrss_user_prefs.value != '-1'
    AND ttrss_feeds.last_updated < NOW() - CAST((ttrss_user_prefs.value || ' minutes') AS INTERVAL))
   OR (ttrss_feeds.update_interval > 0
    AND ttrss_feeds.last_updated < NOW() - CAST((ttrss_feeds.update_interval || ' minutes') AS INTERVAL))
   OR (ttrss_feeds.last_updated IS NULL AND ttrss_user_prefs.value != '-1')
   OR (last_updated = '1970-01-01 00:00:00' AND ttrss_user_prefs.value != '-1'))
  ```

- **10-Minute Stale Lock** (lines 110-114):
  - Feed marked as "being updated" via `last_update_started = NOW()`
  - Prevents concurrent updates: Check `last_update_started < NOW() - INTERVAL '10 minutes'`
  - Query: `AND (ttrss_feeds.last_update_started IS NULL OR ttrss_feeds.last_update_started < NOW() - INTERVAL '10 minutes')`

- **Login Requirement** (lines 72-80):
  - If `DAEMON_UPDATE_LOGIN_LIMIT > 0` and not SINGLE_USER_MODE:
    - Only update feeds for users who logged in within `DAEMON_UPDATE_LOGIN_LIMIT` days
    - Query: `AND ttrss_users.last_login >= NOW() - INTERVAL '".DAEMON_UPDATE_LOGIN_LIMIT." days'`

- **Adaptive Mode** (lines 461-475):
  - If search active: No restriction (empty `view_query_part`)
  - If feed = -1 (starred): No restriction
  - If unread count > 0: Add condition `unread = true AND`
  - Otherwise: No restriction

- **Marked Mode** (lines 477-479):
  - `view_query_part = " marked = true AND "`

- **Published Mode** (lines 485-487):
  - `view_query_part = " published = true AND "`

- **Unread Mode** (lines 489-491, excluding feed -6):
  - `view_query_part = " unread = true AND "`

- **Has Note Mode** (lines 481-483):
  - `view_query_part = " (note IS NOT NULL AND note != '') AND "`

- **Unread_First Mode** (lines 634-636):
  - Modifies order: `$order_by = "unread DESC, $order_by"`
  - Default order: `"score DESC, date_entered DESC, updated DESC"`

### 6. ARTICLE PURGING

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php`

- **Purge Interval Determination** (lines 209-291):
  - Per-feed purge_interval checked first (line 211): `feed_purge_interval($feed_id)`
  - Falls back to user preference if feed interval = 0/NULL

- **Purge Unread Setting** (lines 233-239):
  - If `FORCE_ARTICLE_PURGE = 0`: Check user pref `PURGE_UNREAD_ARTICLES`
  - If `FORCE_ARTICLE_PURGE != 0`: Force purge, ignore user pref
  - If `PURGE_UNREAD_ARTICLES = false`: Add condition `unread = false AND` to spare unread

- **Purge Logic** (lines 248-280):
  - Delete from `ttrss_user_entries` WHERE:
    - `marked = false` (ALWAYS keep marked/starred articles)
    - `feed_id = '$feed_id'` (per-feed purging)
    - `unread = false` (if setting enabled)
    - `ttrss_entries.date_updated < NOW() - INTERVAL '$purge_interval days'` (age-based)

- **Kept Articles**:
  - Starred articles (`marked = true`) NEVER purged
  - Unread articles kept if `PURGE_UNREAD_ARTICLES = true`

- **Cache Invalidation** (line 284):
  - `ccache_update($feed_id, $owner_uid)` called after purge

### 7. CATCHUP OPERATION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php`

- **Function Signature** (line 1094):
  - `catchup_feed($feed, $cat_view, $owner_uid = false, $max_id = false, $mode = 'all')`

- **Mode Parameter** (lines 1104-1128):
  - `1day`: Only articles older than 1 day
  - `1week`: Only articles older than 1 week
  - `2week`: Only articles older than 2 weeks
  - `all` (default): All articles

- **Category Catchup** (lines 1131-1151):
  - If `$feed >= 0` and `$cat_view = true`:
    - If feed > 0: Get children categories: `getChildCategories($feed, $owner_uid)`
    - If feed = 0: Root/uncategorized: `cat_id IS NULL`
    - Update: `SET unread = false, last_read = NOW()`

- **Special Feed Catchup** (lines 1153-1224):
  - `-1` (Starred): `marked = true`
  - `-2` (Published): `published = true`
  - `-3` (Fresh): Articles within `FRESH_ARTICLE_MAX_AGE` hours
  - `-4` (All Articles): All articles (no date restriction)
  - Labels: `feed < LABEL_BASE_INDEX` → use `feed_to_label_id()` conversion

- **Regular Feed Catchup** (lines 1161-1167):
  - `feed_id = $feed`

- **Cache Update** (line 1226):
  - `ccache_update($feed, $owner_uid, $cat_view)` called after catchup

### 9. PUBSUBHUBBUB IMPLEMENTATION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/lib/pubsubhubbub/subscriber.php`

- **Feature Flag** (line 494):
  - Check: `if ($pubsub_state != 2 && PUBSUBHUBBUB_ENABLED)`

- **Subscription Lifecycle** (lines 494-540):
  - Extract hub URL from feed: `$rss->get_links('hub')`
  - Extract self URL: `$rss->get_links('self')`
  - Conditions for subscription:
    - Hub URL found
    - Self URL found
    - curl_init available
    - `open_basedir` not restricted
  - Create Subscriber instance: `new Subscriber($feed_hub_url, $callback_url)`
  - Send subscription: `$s->subscribe($feed_self_url)`
  - Callback URL: `/public.php?op=pubsub&id=$feed`
  - Set state: `pubsub_state = 1` (pending)

- **State Values**:
  - `pubsub_state = 0`: Not subscribed
  - `pubsub_state = 1`: Subscription pending
  - `pubsub_state = 2`: Active subscription

- **Implementation**: Uses external library at `/lib/pubsubhubbub/subscriber.php`
  - Subscriber class handles HTTP POST to hub with mode, callback, topic, verify token
  - Requires curl

### 10. FEED CREDENTIAL ENCRYPTION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/crypt.php`

- **Encryption Flag** (line 232):
  - `$auth_pass_encrypted = sql_bool_to_bool(db_fetch_result($result, 0, "auth_pass_encrypted"))`

- **Decryption on Fetch** (lines 241-244):
  - If `auth_pass_encrypted = true`:
    ```php
    require_once "crypt.php";
    $auth_pass = decrypt_string($auth_pass);
    ```

- **Encryption Method** (crypt.php, lines 22-35):
  - Algorithm: MCRYPT_RIJNDAEL_128 (AES-128)
  - Mode: MCRYPT_MODE_CBC
  - Key: SHA256 hash of `FEED_CRYPT_KEY` constant
  - IV: Random, generated per encryption
  - Format: `base64(IV):base64(ciphertext)`

- **Decryption Method** (crypt.php, lines 2-20):
  - Split on `:` to extract IV and ciphertext
  - Decode from base64
  - Decrypt using same key derivation
  - Return trimmed plaintext

- **Storage**:
  - `auth_login`: Stored plaintext
  - `auth_pass`: Encrypted if `auth_pass_encrypted = true`, plaintext otherwise

### 11. LABEL SYSTEM

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/labels.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions2.php`

- **Label ID Mapping** (functions2.php, lines 2400-2406):
  - `LABEL_BASE_INDEX = -1024` (functions.php, line 5)
  - Label feed ID formula: `label_to_feed_id($label) = LABEL_BASE_INDEX - 1 - abs($label)`
  - Reverse: `feed_to_label_id($feed) = LABEL_BASE_INDEX - 1 + abs($feed)`
  - Example: Label with DB ID 1 → Feed ID -1026
  - Range: Feed IDs below -1024 represent labels

- **Label Cache** (labels.php, lines 14-57):
  - Cache stored in `ttrss_user_entries.label_cache` as JSON
  - Format: Array of [feed_id, caption, fg_color, bg_color] tuples
  - Special value: `["no-labels" => 1]` indicates no labels
  - Lazy-loaded: Fetched from `ttrss_user_labels2` if cache empty
  - Populated via `label_update_cache($owner_uid, $id, $labels)`

- **Label Retrieval** (labels.php, lines 72-82):
  - `get_all_labels($owner_uid)`: Returns array of label objects
  - Query: `SELECT fg_color, bg_color, caption FROM ttrss_labels2 WHERE owner_uid = $owner_uid`

- **Label Operations**:
  - Create: `label_create($caption, $fg_color, $bg_color, $owner_uid)`
  - Add to article: `label_add_article($id, $label, $owner_uid)` → `ttrss_user_labels2`
  - Remove from article: `label_remove_article($id, $label, $owner_uid)`
  - Delete label: `label_remove($id, $owner_uid)` (also removes associated access keys)

### 13. SESSION VALIDATION

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/sessions.php`

- **Validation Function** (lines 39-102):
  - Called in each request to validate current session

- **Validation Checks** (in order):
  1. **SINGLE_USER_MODE**: Skip all checks if enabled (line 40)
  2. **Version Check** (line 42): `VERSION_STATIC` must match `$_SESSION["version"]`
  3. **IP Address Check** (lines 44-63):
     - `SESSION_CHECK_ADDRESS` setting determines strictness:
       - 0: Disabled (empty string)
       - 1: Match first 3 octets (e.g., 192.168.1.*)
       - 2: Match first 2 octets (e.g., 192.168.*)
     - Comparison: `strpos($_SERVER['REMOTE_ADDR'], $check_ip) !== 0`
  4. **Schema Version Check** (lines 65-69): `ref_schema_version` must match current schema
  5. **User Agent Check** (lines 71-75): SHA1 of `HTTP_USER_AGENT` must match session value
  6. **User Existence Check** (lines 77-98): User row must exist in `ttrss_users`
  7. **Password Hash Check** (lines 89-97): Password hash must not have changed

- **Session Invalidation Errors**:
  - Sets `$_SESSION["login_error_msg"]` with specific reason
  - Returns `false` to deny access

- **Session Storage** (lines 105-157):
  - Custom session handler: `ttrss_read/write/destroy/gc`
  - Sessions stored in `ttrss_sessions` table
  - Data base64-encoded
  - Garbage collection: Removes rows where `expire < NOW()`

### 15. SPECIAL FEED IDS

**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php`
**File:** `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions2.php`

- **Standard Virtual Feeds** (functions2.php, lines 554-630):
  - **-1**: Starred (marked) articles
    - Query: `marked = true`
    - Order: `last_marked DESC, date_entered DESC, updated DESC`
    - Allows archived articles
  
  - **-2**: Published articles (non-category view)
    - Query: `published = true`
    - Order: `last_published DESC, date_entered DESC, updated DESC`
    - Allows archived articles
    - (Also used as labels category in category view)
  
  - **-3**: Fresh articles (within configured hours)
    - Query: `unread = true AND score >= 0 AND date_entered > NOW() - INTERVAL '$FRESH_ARTICLE_MAX_AGE hour'`
    - Max age set by `FRESH_ARTICLE_MAX_AGE` pref
  
  - **-4**: All articles
    - Query: `true` (no restrictions)
    - Allows archived articles
  
  - **-6**: Recently read
    - Query: `unread = false AND last_read IS NOT NULL`
    - Order: `last_read DESC`
    - Allows archived articles
    - Disables vfeed grouping

  - **0** (in cat_view): Uncategorized feeds
    - Query: `cat_id IS NULL AND feed_id IS NOT NULL`

  - **0** (non-cat): Archive (feed_id IS NULL)
    - Query: `feed_id IS NULL`

- **Label Range** (functions.php, line 5 + functions2.php, line 617):
  - **< -1024** (LABEL_BASE_INDEX): Represents labels
  - Conversion: `feed_to_label_id($feed)` / `label_to_feed_id($label_id)`

- **Plugin Feed Range** (functions.php, line 6):
  - **PLUGIN_FEED_BASE_INDEX = -128**: Reserved for plugins

- **Category Feeds** (functions2.php, lines 1131-1151):
  - **Positive IDs** (1+): Real feed IDs in category view
  - **0**: Root/uncategorized category

## 2. errors.php - Error Codes and Messages

| Code | Message | Meaning |
|------|---------|---------|
| 0 | (blank) | No error |
| 1 | "This program requires XmlHttpRequest..." | Browser lacks AJAX support |
| 2 | "This program requires cookies..." | Browser cookies disabled |
| 3 | "Backend sanity check failed" | Server configuration invalid |
| 4 | "Frontend sanity check failed" | JavaScript check failed |
| 5 | "Incorrect database schema version..." | DB upgrade needed |
| 6 | "Request not authorized" | Auth failure |
| 7 | "No operation to perform" | Empty request |
| 8 | "Could not display feed..." | Feed query failed or label syntax error |
| 8 (reassigned) | "Denied. Your access level is insufficient..." | Insufficient permissions (NOTE: overwrites code 8) |
| 9 | "Configuration check failed" | Config validation error |
| 10 | "Your version of MySQL is not currently supported..." | Unsupported MySQL version |
| 11 | "[This error is not returned by server]" | Reserved |
| 12 | "SQL escaping test failed..." | Database/PHP security issue |

**Note:** Error code 8 is defined twice; second definition overwrites the first.

---

## 3. include/sanity_check.php - Validation Rules

### Configuration Requirements
- **config.php exists** - Config file mandatory
- **PLUGINS contains auth_*** - At least one auth plugin enabled
- **Not running as root** - Security check
- **PHP version >= 5.3.0** - Minimum version
- **CONFIG_VERSION == EXPECTED_CONFIG_VERSION** - Config version match
- **SINGLE_USER_MODE requirement** - If enabled, admin user (id=1) must exist

### File/Directory Permissions
- **CACHE_DIR/images** - Must be writable
- **CACHE_DIR/upload** - Must be writable
- **CACHE_DIR/export** - Must be writable
- **CACHE_DIR/js** - Must be writable
- **ICONS_DIR** - Must be writable
- **LOCK_DIRECTORY** - Must be writable

### Configuration Value Validation
- **FEED_CRYPT_KEY length** - Must be exactly 24 chars if set
- **FEED_CRYPT_KEY + mcrypt** - mcrypt required if key is set
- **GENERATED_CONFIG_CHECK == EXPECTED_CONFIG_VERSION** - sanity_config.php must be current
- **SELF_URL_PATH** - Must not be default "http://example.org/tt-rss/"

### PHP Extensions Required
- **curl_init OR allow_url_fopen** - For remote feed fetching
- **json_encode** - JSON support mandatory
- **mysql_connect OR mysqli_connect** - For MySQL
- **pg_connect** - For PostgreSQL
- **mb_strlen** - Multibyte string support
- **hash()** - Hash function support
- **ctype_lower** - Character type functions (HTMLPurifier requirement)
- **DOMDocument** - XML DOM parsing

### Optional Feature Dependencies
- **PUBSUBHUBBUB (HUB or ENABLED)** - Requires curl_init
- **SPHINX_ENABLED** - Must NOT have system-wide Sphinx client (conflicts)

## 5. install/index.php - Installer Workflow

### Installation Steps

**Phase 1: Database Configuration Form**
- Database type selection (PostgreSQL or MySQL)
- Username input
- Password input
- Database name input
- Host name (optional)
- Port (optional hints: 3306 MySQL, 5432 PostgreSQL)
- Submits to: `op=testconfig`

**Phase 2: Sanity Checks** (`op=testconfig`)
- PHP version >= 5.3.0
- curl_init OR allow_url_fopen
- json_encode support
- MySQL (mysql_connect OR mysqli_connect) OR PostgreSQL (pg_connect)
- mb_strlen support
- hash() support
- ctype_lower support
- iconv support (charset handling)
- DOMDocument support
- Optional notices if curl missing

**Phase 3: Database Connection Test**
- Attempts connection with provided credentials
- Verifies ttrss_feeds table existence
- If tables exist: warns data will be removed, requires confirmation
- If no tables: allows direct initialization

**Phase 4: Database Initialization** (`op=installschema`)
- Reads schema file: `schema/ttrss_schema_[pgsql|mysql].sql`
- Executes SQL statements (splits by `;`, skips comments)
- Alternative: Skip schema initialization

**Phase 5: Config File Generation**
- Reads `config.php-dist` as template
- Replaces DB_* and SELF_URL_PATH values
- Auto-generates FEED_CRYPT_KEY (24 chars) if mcrypt available
- Displays config in textarea
- Auto-saves to `../config.php` if directory writable
- Manual copy option if not writable

**Phase 6: Completion**
- Default credentials: username=`admin`, password=`password`
- Warning to change password immediately
- Users must login once within 24 hours or account deleted

### Database Operations
- Creates schema via SQL execution
- No admin user creation in installer (uses default DB schema)
- Optional schema skip for existing databases

---

## 6. register.php - User Registration Flow

### Features
- **Feed endpoint** (`format=feed`): XML feed showing available registration slots
- **Availability check** (`action=check`): AJAX XML response checking username availability
- **Auto-cleanup**: Deletes unlogged-in users older than 24 hours

### Registration Form Fields
1. **Desired login** (required) - Username with availability check
2. **Email** (required) - Valid email address
3. **CAPTCHA** (required) - "How much is two plus two" (Turing test)

### Validation Rules
- All three fields required (login, email, turing_test)
- CAPTCHA answer: "four" OR "4" accepted
- Username lowercase conversion: `mb_strtolower()`
- Username uniqueness check
- Email case-insensitive storage

### Registration Process
1. User validation (all fields, CAPTCHA pass)
2. Check username not already taken
3. Auto-generate random password: `make_password()` (8 chars from safe set)
4. Create password hash with salt: `encrypt_password($password, $salt, true)`
5. Insert user: `ttrss_users` table with `access_level=0` (subscriber)
6. Initialize user: `initialize_user($new_uid)`
7. Send two emails:
   - **To user**: Login credentials + login-within-24-hours warning
   - **To admin** (REG_NOTIFY_ADDRESS): New registration notice

### Email Templates
- Uses `classes/ttrssmailer.php`
- Method: `quickMail(email, login, subject, html_body, text_body)`

### Configuration Constants Used
- ENABLE_REGISTRATION - Master switch
- REG_MAX_USERS - Enrollment cap (0=unlimited)
- REG_NOTIFY_ADDRESS - Admin notification email
- DIGEST_SUBJECT (implied for SMTP config)

### User Auto-Deletion
- Trigger: `last_login IS NULL AND created < NOW() - INTERVAL '1 day' AND access_level = 0`
- Database-specific:
  - PostgreSQL: `NOW() - INTERVAL '1 day'`
  - MySQL: `DATE_SUB(NOW(), INTERVAL 1 DAY)`

---

## 7. classes/opml.php - OPML Import/Export

### Export Features

**Format:** OPML 1.0 XML with:
- Standard OPML metadata (dateCreated, title)
- Feed hierarchy with categories
- Optional settings/preferences/labels/filters export
- Version: SCHEMA_VERSION included in export

**Export Content:**
- **Feeds**: title, feed_url (xmlUrl), site_url (htmlUrl), category hierarchy
- **Settings** (optional): `ttrss_user_prefs` as outline elements with pref-name/value
- **Labels** (optional): `ttrss_labels2` with label-name, label-fg-color, label-bg-color
- **Filters** (optional): `ttrss_filters2` complex JSON encoding with rules and actions

**Duplicate Handling (Export):**
- Private feeds excluded if hide_private_feeds=true (checks: private=false, auth_login='', auth_pass='')
- Empty categories removed via XPath/DOMDocument cleanup

**Methods:**
- `opml_export($name, $owner_uid, $hide_private_feeds, $include_settings)`
- `opml_export_category($owner_uid, $cat_id, $hide_private_feeds)` - Recursive

---

### Import Features

**File Upload:**
- Uses `$_FILES['opml_file']`
- Validates upload success (`$_FILES['error'] != 0`)
- Temp file in CACHE_DIR/upload
- Parsed via DOMDocument::load()

**Import Categories:**
- Auto-creates "Imported feeds" default category via `add_feed_category()`
- Creates subcategories recursively via `get_feed_category()` and `add_feed_category()`
- Handles parent-child hierarchy

**Duplicate Handling (Import):**
- Feeds: Checks `ttrss_feeds` for feed_url + owner_uid match
  - Duplicate: Shows notice, skips import
  - New: Inserts with title, feed_url, site_url, cat_id
- Labels: Checks `label_find_id()` for duplicates
  - Duplicate: Shows notice, skips
  - New: Creates via `label_create()`
- Preferences: Simple `set_pref()` overwrite (no duplicate check)
- Filters: Uses transactions; supports rules and actions restoration

**Special Categories** (not created as real categories):
- `"tt-rss-prefs"` - Preferences outline section
- `"tt-rss-labels"` - Labels outline section
- `"tt-rss-filters"` - Filters outline section (filter-type="2" only)

**Methods:**
- `opml_import($owner_uid)` - Main entry point
- `opml_import_category($doc, $root_node, $owner_uid, $parent_id)` - Recursive processor
- `opml_import_feed($doc, $node, $cat_id, $owner_uid)`
- `opml_import_label($doc, $node, $owner_uid)`
- `opml_import_preference($doc, $node, $owner_uid)`
- `opml_import_filter($doc, $node, $owner_uid)` - JSON filter format

**Output:** HTML progress notices during import

---

## 8. include/digest.php - Email Digest System

### Digest Sending (`send_headlines_digests()`)

**Triggers:**
- Called from update daemon or cron
- Processes max 15 users per batch
- Selects users where `email != '' AND (last_digest_sent IS NULL OR last_digest_sent < NOW() - 1 DAY)`

**Timing Logic:**
- User preference: `DIGEST_PREFERRED_TIME` (time string like "00:00")
- Window: Sends within 2 hours of preferred time
- Condition: `time() >= preferred_ts AND time() - preferred_ts <= 7200`

**Content Assembly (`prepare_headlines_digest($user_id, $days=1, $limit=1000`)**
- Days: Last N days of articles (default 1)
- Limit: Max 1000 headlines per digest
- Filters: `include_in_digest=true AND unread=true AND score>=0`
- Sort: By category > feed > score DESC > date DESC
- Optional catchup: Marks digested articles as read (DIGEST_CATCHUP preference)

**Templates Used:**
1. `templates/digest_template_html.txt` - HTML version
2. `templates/digest_template.txt` - Text version

**Template Variables:**
- CUR_DATE (Y/m/d format)
- CUR_TIME (G:i format)
- FEED_TITLE
- ARTICLE_TITLE
- ARTICLE_LINK
- ARTICLE_UPDATED
- ARTICLE_EXCERPT (truncated 300 chars, tags stripped)

**Template Blocks:**
- `{article}` - Repeating article entries
- `{feed}` - Feed grouping separator
- `{digest}` - Outer digest container

**Email Sending:**
- Class: `ttrssMailer`
- Method: `quickMail($email, $login, DIGEST_SUBJECT, $html_digest, $text_digest)`
- Updates: `ttrss_users.last_digest_sent = NOW()`

**Database Queries:**
- PostgreSQL: `NOW() - INTERVAL '1 days'`, `NOW() - INTERVAL '$days days'`
- MySQL: `DATE_SUB(NOW(), INTERVAL 1 DAY)`, `DATE_SUB(NOW(), INTERVAL $days DAY)`

**Preferences Used:**
- DIGEST_ENABLE - Master switch per user
- DIGEST_PREFERRED_TIME - Scheduled send time
- DIGEST_CATCHUP - Auto-mark as read
- ENABLE_FEED_CATS - Category display in digest
- USER_TIMEZONE - User timezone conversion

---

|----------|---------|------|
| **digest_template_html.txt** | HTML-formatted digest email body | Email HTML |

**Template Engine:** MiniTemplator class (`lib/MiniTemplator.class.php`)

**Variable Substitution Pattern:** `{VARIABLE_NAME}` blocks and repeating sections

## 10. update.php - CLI Update Script

### Supported Commands

| Command | Function | Purpose |
|---------|----------|---------|
| `--feeds` | `update_daemon_common()` | Update all feeds once, then housekeeping |
| `--daemon` | Loop + `--daemon-loop` | Infinite daemon mode with DAEMON_SLEEP_INTERVAL sleep |
| `--daemon-loop` | `update_daemon_common()` + hooks | Single daemon iteration |
| `--feedbrowser` | `update_feedbrowser_cache()` | Update feed directory cache |
| `--force-update` | DB query | Mark all feeds with 1970-01-01 (force refresh) |
| `--cleanup-tags` | `cleanup_tags(14, 50000)` | Remove old tags; 14-day threshold, 50K max |
| `--task N` | Lock management | Task ID for multi-process coordination |
| `--pidlock PID` | Lock management | PID-based locking for concurrent processes |
| `--quiet` | Silent mode | Suppress stdout messages |
| `--log FILE` | Logging | Log to specified file instead of stdout |
| `--indexes` | DB index rebuild | Recreate missing schema indexes (interactive) |
| `--update-schema` | `DbUpdater` | Migrate database schema (interactive) |
| `--convert-filters` | Filter migration | Convert old type1 filters to type2 (interactive) |
| `--list-plugins` | Plugin listing | List all available plugins with versions |
| `--help` | Help text | Display command reference |
| **Plugin Commands** | `PluginHost::get_commands()` | Dynamic plugin-provided commands |

### Execution Flow

1. **Startup:**
   - Requires PHP CLI (not CGI)
   - Disables sessions: `define('DISABLE_SESSIONS', true)`
   - Loads config, DB, functions, plugins

2. **Lock Management:**
   - Standard: `update.lock`
   - Daemon: `update_daemon.lock`
   - With task: `update.lock-task_N`
   - With PID: `update_daemon-PID.lock`
   - Location: `LOCK_DIRECTORY`
   - Prevents concurrent runs

3. **Daemon Mode (`--daemon`):**
   - Infinite loop
   - Spawns child: `PHP_EXECUTABLE update.php --daemon-loop [quiet] [log]`
   - Sleeps: `DAEMON_SLEEP_INTERVAL` seconds between iterations
   - Can specify quiet/log flags

4. **Schema Validation:**
   - Skipped if `--update-schema` flag
   - Otherwise: `$schema_version != SCHEMA_VERSION` → die

5. **Plugin Integration:**
   - Hook: `PluginHost::HOOK_UPDATE_TASK` / `hook_update_task`
   - Runs after feed/daemon operations

6. **Interactive Operations** (require user confirmation):
   - `--indexes` - "yes" to continue
   - `--update-schema` - "yes" to continue
   - `--convert-filters` - "yes" to continue

### Database Queries (Task-Specific)

**Force Update (`--force-update`):**
```sql
UPDATE ttrss_feeds SET last_update_started = '1970-01-01', last_updated = '1970-01-01'
```

**Index Recreation:**
- PostgreSQL: Queries `pg_catalog.pg_class` for index names
- MySQL: Queries `information_schema.statistics`
- Drops and recreates via SQL schema file

**Filter Conversion (`--convert-filters`):**
- Deletes `ttrss_filters2` (old type2 filters)
- Iterates `ttrss_filters` (old type1)
- Skips date filters (type 5)
- Converts to new JSON format

**Schema Update (`--update-schema`):**
- Uses `DbUpdater` class with `Db::get()`
- Incremental: `$i = getSchemaVersion() + 1` to `SCHEMA_VERSION`
- Calls `performUpdateTo($i)` for each version

### Configuration Constants Used
- PHP_EXECUTABLE - CLI binary path
- DAEMON_SLEEP_INTERVAL - Daemon loop sleep duration
- DAEMON_FEED_LIMIT - Feeds per daemon iteration
- LOCK_DIRECTORY - Lockfile location
- PLUGINS - Plugin list
- DB_TYPE, SCHEMA_VERSION - Database config
- QUIET mode - Output suppression

---

### 4. FEED REDIRECT HANDLING

**File: `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php:374-375`**

**Redirect Behavior:**
- Line 374: `CURLOPT_FOLLOWLOCATION` set to `!ini_get("safe_mode") && !ini_get("open_basedir")`
- Line 375: `CURLOPT_MAXREDIRS` = 20 (handles up to 20 sequential redirects)
- **CRITICAL EDGE CASE**: Curl follows redirects automatically, but feed_url is NOT updated
  - Final URL is transparent to application
  - If 301/302 redirects feed to new URL, the original `feed_url` stored in DB remains unchanged
  - **Potential Issue**: Feed could be migrated to new URL, but DB still references old URL

**Site URL Update (rssfuncs.php:419-474):**
- Line 419: `site_url = rewrite_relative_url($fetch_url, $rss->get_link())`
- Lines 471-473: Site URL updated if changed from original
- **Note**: Feed URL itself is never updated on redirect

**Output Encoding:**
- Line 111: `sanitize($line["content"], false, $owner_uid)`
- Line 161: HTML entities encoded with `htmlspecialchars()`
- Content is cleaned and escaped

---

### 9. CONCURRENT OPERATIONS & RACE CONDITIONS

**Feed Update Locking (rssfuncs.php:109-115):**
- Line 111-114: Checks `last_update_started` timestamp
- Threshold: 10 minutes (PostgreSQL: INTERVAL '10 minutes', MySQL: INTERVAL 10 MINUTE)
- Line 154-155: Updates `last_update_started = NOW()` BEFORE fetch

**Potential Race Conditions:**
- If two daemon processes both see feed not updated, both could fetch simultaneously
- Lock is timestamp-based, not atomic
- Window between lock check and update could allow duplicate fetches

**Concurrent Mark-as-Read (functions2.php:1032-1040):**
- No explicit locking mechanism
- Updates are SQL-based: `UPDATE ttrss_user_entries SET unread = false WHERE ...`
- Database ACID guarantees handle atomicity, but no application-level concurrency control

**Transaction Usage (rssfuncs.php:709, 824, 973):**
- Line 709: `db_query("BEGIN")`
- Line 824, 973: `db_query("COMMIT")`
- Transactions isolate article updates during feed processing

---

### 10. FEED DELETION CASCADE

**Schema Cascade Behavior (ttrss_schema_mysql.sql:193-195):**

```sql
foreign key (ref_id) references ttrss_entries(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
foreign key (feed_id) references ttrss_feeds(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
```

**When feed is deleted:**
1. All `ttrss_user_entries` rows referencing that feed are deleted
2. However, `ttrss_entries` rows (shared articles) are NOT deleted
3. Orphan `ttrss_entries` remain if:
   - Only 1 user had subscribed to that feed
   - `ON DELETE CASCADE` on `ref_id` only deletes user_entries, not base entries

**Orphan Cleanup:**
- No explicit cleanup code found
- Orphaned entries remain in database indefinitely
- No foreign key constraint prevents orphan ttrss_entries

---

### 11. TIMEZONE HANDLING

**File: `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/functions.php:891-961`**

**convert_timestamp() (lines 891-907):**
- Creates DateTimeZone objects from string identifiers
- Line 894-896: Try-catch with fallback to UTC on invalid timezone
- Line 905-906: Calculates offset and adjusts timestamp

**make_local_datetime() (lines 909-953):**
- Line 912: Gets user's timezone: `get_pref('USER_TIMEZONE', $owner_uid)`
- Line 913: Defaults invalid timestamp to 1970-01-01
- Lines 920-941: Converts to user timezone using DateTimeZone
- Line 943: Delegates to `smart_date_time()` unless `$no_smart_dt = true`

**smart_date_time() (lines 955-962):**
- Line 958: Compares date with current date (with timezone offset)
- Same day: shows only time (e.g., "14:30")
- Same year: shows month/day (e.g., "Mar 15")
- Different year: shows full date (e.g., "2024-03-15")

**Feed Timestamp Processing (rssfuncs.php:566-576):**
- Line 566: `$entry_timestamp = $item->get_date()`
- Line 570: If invalid/future timestamp, defaults to `time()`
- Line 574: Formats with `strftime()` in UTC

---

- Line 7: `ttrss_linked_instances` table

**File: `/Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/themes/`**

**Theme Loading (functions2.php:20):**
- Line 20: `$params["theme"] = get_pref("USER_CSS_THEME", false, false)`
- Retrieved from user preferences

**Available Themes:**
- Located in `/themes/` directory
- Feedly theme: `/themes/tt-rss-feedly-theme/feedly.css`
- Theme structure: CSS files + optional subdirectories

**Theme Selection:**
- User preference stored in DB
- Loaded via `get_pref()` function
- Applied client-side (CSS theme switching)

## ROUND 2 COMPLIANCE REVIEW -- REMAINING FLAWS

### CATEGORY 1: INTERNAL INCONSISTENCIES (cross-reference mismatches between files)

**1.1 AGENTS.md ADR filenames do not match actual filenames on disk.**
AGENTS.md line 34 lists `0006-orm-vs-raw-sql.md`. The actual file on disk is `0006-orm-strategy.md`. AGENTS.md line 38 lists `0008-password-hash-migration.md`. The actual file is `0008-password-migration.md`. AGENTS.md line 39 lists `0009-feed-credential-encryption.md` (matches). AGENTS.md line 40 lists `0010-plugin-system-implementation.md`. The actual file is `0010-plugin-system.md`. AGENTS.md line 41 lists `0011-background-worker-architecture.md`. The actual file is `0011-background-worker.md`. Five of the ten new ADR filenames in AGENTS.md are wrong. A developer following AGENTS.md to locate files will get "file not found" errors.

**1.2 Project charter Solution Space table states decisions as facts; all ADRs say "TBD".**
The charter (spec 00, lines 79-93) presents 15 rows of definitive decisions: "Flask", "PostgreSQL only", "Celery with Redis broker", "feedparser library", "httpx (async-capable)", etc. Every ADR has `Decision: TBD` in its body. The Solution Space table should say "Preliminary Recommendation" or "Proposed", not bare nouns implying accepted decisions. This is a structural contradiction: the governing document asserts decisions that the decision records explicitly declare as not yet made.

**1.3 ADR-0001 references wrong spec file.**
ADR-0001 line 10 says "Five flow variants were analyzed in `specs/09-migration-dimensions.md`." The migration dimensions spec is `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md`. Spec 09 is the source-code index.

**1.4 ADR-0008 states the wrong PHP hash format.**
ADR-0008 Context section says the password hash format is `sha1:salt:hash`. The actual PHP code (spec 11, business rule 20, and `functions2.php:1481-1489` per spec 06) uses `SHA1:<hash>` for unsalted and `MODE2:<hash>` for salted SHA256. The format `sha1:salt:hash` is fabricated and does not appear in the source code. A developer relying on this ADR will implement the wrong hash verification logic.

**1.5 ADR-0008 mentions MD5 hashes with no source evidence.**
ADR-0008 says "Some older records may use unsalted MD5." No spec document or source file reference supports this claim. Spec 06 mentions only SHA1 and SHA256. This is an unverified assertion in a security-critical ADR.

**1.6 Cross-reference table in charter maps P1 (RSS parsing) to spec 07-caching-performance.**
Premise P1 concerns RSS parsing libraries. Spec 07 covers caching and performance. The relevant specs are 01-architecture (which documents the FeedParser hierarchy) and the feed processing classes in 09-source-index. The cross-reference is wrong.

**1.7 Cross-reference table maps P8 (i18n/gettext) to spec 08-deployment.**
P8 concerns Python gettext compatibility with existing .po/.mo files. While deployment spec 08 mentions i18n in passing (line 164-166), there is no dedicated i18n spec. The mapping to 08-deployment is a stretch and obscures the fact that i18n has no proper spec coverage.

**1.8 Testing strategy (spec 12) references MySQL alongside PostgreSQL.**
Spec 12 line 160 says schema parity should be compared against both `ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql` and `ttrss_schema_mysql.sql`. Spec 12 line 239-245 provisions a MySQL 8.0 test container. But ADR-0003 recommends PostgreSQL-only, and the charter Solution Space table states "PostgreSQL only" as the decision. Either spec 12 is inconsistent with the charter or the dual-DB testing is intentional and contradicts the single-DB constraint (C7).

**1.9 Testing strategy label ID conversion formulas are wrong.**
Spec 12 line 44 states: `label_to_feed_id(N) -> -(N + 11)` and `feed_to_label_id(N) -> -(N) - 11`. The actual formulas from spec 11 (lines 409-415) are `label_to_feed_id(id) = LABEL_BASE_INDEX - 1 - abs(id)` which is `-1024 - 1 - abs(id)`, and the inverse. These are not the same as `-(N+11)`. The test spec contains incorrect expected values.

### CATEGORY 2: STILL MISSING (gaps that block a developer)

**2.1 No function-level inventory.**
Requirements state "Include function inventory." Spec 09 is a file-level inventory. No spec contains a function-level inventory mapping PHP functions to their purpose, parameters, return types, and Python equivalents. The approximately 100+ standalone functions in `functions.php` and `functions2.php` are not enumerated. A developer migrating `functions.php` has no checklist of what must be ported.

**2.2 PHP-to-Python mapping is incomplete and scattered.**
Requirement 8 demands "PHP pattern -> Python equivalent with concrete library choices." Spec 10 (Dimension 6, lines 140-153) has a 12-row table of pattern mappings. This is a skeletal summary, not a comprehensive mapping. Missing patterns include: PHP `unserialize()` (used in plugin storage), PHP `mail()` / PHPMailer -> Python equivalent, `SimplePie` -> `feedparser` mapping of specific API calls, `preg_match` flag differences, `DOMDocument` -> `lxml` element access patterns, `mcrypt` -> `cryptography` API mapping, `gettext` -> Python `gettext` API mapping, PHP array functions -> Python equivalents, PHP `pcntl_fork` -> Celery task model, PHP `flock` -> Python locking. The requirement asks for concrete mappings; what exists is a high-level placeholder.

**2.3 No mapping of PHP configuration constants to Python environment variables.**
Spec 01 lists 38 configuration constants (lines 350-393). Spec 12 line 70 says "All 38 constants from config.php-dist have Python equivalents." But no spec provides the actual mapping table showing each PHP constant's Python environment variable name, type, default value, and validation rule. A developer implementing config loading has no specification to work from.

**2.4 No specification for user preference system.**
The `ttrss_prefs` table contains 40+ system preferences with default values (spec 02 line 191 mentions "40+ system preferences"). No spec enumerates all 40+ preference names, their types, default values, and which code consumes them. This is business-critical data (view modes, purge intervals, digest settings all depend on preferences) that a developer cannot reconstruct without reading the PHP source.

**2.5 No specification for the installer/setup wizard.**
`ttrss/install/index.php` is listed in spec 09 (line 211) but has zero spec coverage. The installer creates the initial database schema, generates `config.php`, and sets up the admin user. Whether this functionality is in scope for migration is not stated.

**2.6 No specification for `update.php` CLI commands.**
Spec 03 lists `ttrss/update.php` as a "CLI update tool" (line 12) but does not document its subcommands, arguments, or behavior. ADR-0011 mentions it briefly. A developer implementing the CLI equivalent has no spec to work from.

**2.7 No specification for email digest template rendering.**
Spec 11 (business rule 18) documents digest query logic but does not specify the MiniTemplator template engine behavior that must be replicated. The template variables are listed (line 806) but the rendering logic (variable substitution, iteration over articles, HTML vs plain text formatting) is not specified.

**2.8 No specification for `image.php` proxy behavior.**
Spec 09 lists `image.php` and spec 07 mentions image caching, but there is no spec for the image proxy's URL routing, cache lookup, X-Sendfile header generation, content-type detection, or error handling.

**2.9 No spec for `register.php` form validation beyond CAPTCHA.**
Spec 11 (business rule 20) covers registration but does not specify the HTML form itself, field validation rules (e.g., minimum username length, email format validation), or the email template for temporary passwords.

**2.10 Schema files are never verified against spec claims.**
Spec 02 claims 35 tables. Spec 02 lists tables in sections, and the total count across all sections is 35 including 3 deprecated tables. Whether the deprecated tables should be modeled in Python is not stated. The distinction matters: if deprecated tables are excluded, only 32 tables need SQLAlchemy models, contradicting the repeated "35 tables" claim throughout all specs.

### CATEGORY 3: STILL OVER-ENGINEERED

**3.1 Five migration flow variants in spec 10 with detailed phase breakdowns.**
ADR-0001 already distills these to a recommendation. Spec 10 retains 150+ lines of variant descriptions (lines 157-303) that are redundant with the ADR. The recommendation matrix (lines 342-352) duplicates ADR-0001's analysis.

**3.2 Dijit widget inventory in spec 04 (lines 164-189).**
The dijit widget list and custom extension list in spec 04 document the existing frontend that ADR-0004 says should be kept unchanged. Since the frontend is not being migrated in Phase 1, this inventory serves no migration purpose. It documents a library that will be served as static files.

**3.3 Docker compose test environment for MySQL in spec 12.**
If PostgreSQL-only is the decision (ADR-0003, charter), the MySQL test container (spec 12 lines 239-245) is dead weight.

### CATEGORY 4: NEW PROBLEMS INTRODUCED BY REVISION

**4.1 Spec 11 line number references are for the PHP source files, not for the spec files themselves.**
The requirement states "Whether the new business rules spec (11) actually has verifiable line numbers." Spec 11 does contain line references -- to the PHP source. These references have been verified as accurate (spot-checked GUID construction at rssfuncs.php:550, content hash at rssfuncs.php:707, filter evaluation at rssfuncs.php:1272). This requirement is met. However, the business rules spec makes no reference to which Python module should implement each rule. This is a forward-reference gap.

**4.2 Charter now has a detailed Solution Space table that creates a false sense of finality.**
By listing concrete tools (Flask, PostgreSQL, Celery, feedparser, httpx, Fernet, pluggy) as decided, the charter creates the impression that architectural decisions are settled. But every ADR says `Decision: TBD`. If a developer reads only the charter (as the governing document), they will begin coding with Flask. If they then read ADR-0002, they discover the framework is officially undecided. This is an actively harmful inconsistency introduced by the revision.

**4.3 Testing strategy scoring thresholds are labeled wrong.**
Spec 12 line 40: "Threshold tests at -500 (score_low), 0 (neutral), +500 (score_high), +1000 (score_half_high)." The actual thresholds from spec 11 are: score < -500 auto-marks as read, score > 1000 auto-stars. The display icons (spec 11 lines 167-172) are: > 100 = high, > 0 = half-high, < -100 = low, < 0 = half-low, == 0 = neutral. Spec 12's parenthetical labels ("score_low", "score_high", "score_half_high") do not match the actual icon names or threshold semantics from spec 11.

**4.4 ADR-0007 references `SESSION_EXPIRE_TIME` which is not in the source.**
ADR-0007 says the PHP code has "configurable timeout (`SESSION_EXPIRE_TIME`)." The actual constant is `SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME` (spec 01 line 379). `SESSION_EXPIRE_TIME` does not appear in the configuration constants list.

**4.5 ADR-0011 says `DAEMON_FEED_LIMIT` controls parallel child processes.**
ADR-0011 Context says the daemon "Supports a configurable number of parallel child processes (`DAEMON_FEED_LIMIT`)." Spec 07 line 172 correctly identifies `DAEMON_FEED_LIMIT = 500` as the max feeds per update cycle, not the number of parallel processes. The parallel process count is `MAX_JOBS=2` (spec 07 line 144, spec 01 line 174). The ADR confuses two different constants.

**4.6 ADR-0015 recommends httpx but ADR-0007 recommends Flask.**
Flask is a WSGI (synchronous) framework. httpx's primary value proposition is async support. Running `httpx.AsyncClient` inside Flask requires `asyncio.run()` within a synchronous request handler or Celery task. This architectural tension is not acknowledged in either ADR or in the charter. The ADRs do not cross-reference each other on this point.

**4.7 Spec 07 mentions SimplePie; spec 14 (ADR-0014) says the PHP parser is custom DOMDocument-based.**
Spec 07 line 66-69 describes "SimplePie feed cache" with SHA1-hashed filenames. ADR-0014 says "The PHP codebase uses a custom `FeedParser` class built on PHP's `DOMDocument` XML parser." Spec 08 line 175 lists "SimplePie (implied)" as a bundled library. The actual source uses a custom `FeedParser` class (confirmed in spec 01 lines 109-114). SimplePie is referenced in cache directory names but may not be the actual parser. This contradiction is never resolved: is SimplePie used or not?

**4.8 Source file paths use two different base path conventions.**
Specs 01-08 say "All paths relative to `source-repos/ttrss-php/`." Spec 11 says "All file:line references are relative to `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/`." These are different base paths. A file path like `include/rssfuncs.php` resolves to `source-repos/ttrss-php/include/rssfuncs.php` under one convention and `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/include/rssfuncs.php` under the other. Only the latter exists on disk. Spec 11 is correct; specs 01-08 are wrong -- their file references (e.g., `ttrss/include/functions.php`) only work because they include the `ttrss/` prefix, but the stated base path is the parent directory. This is confusing and inconsistent.

### SUMMARY

- **5 filename mismatches** in AGENTS.md vs actual ADR files on disk
- **1 wrong spec cross-reference** in ADR-0001
- **1 fabricated hash format** in ADR-0008
- **1 wrong constant name** in ADR-0011
- **1 wrong constant name** in ADR-0007
- **1 contradiction** between charter decisions and ADR "TBD" statuses
- **2 incorrect test formulas/labels** in spec 12
- **1 unresolved SimplePie vs DOMDocument contradiction** across specs
- **2 inconsistent base path conventions** across spec files
- **10 missing specifications** that would block implementation
- **3 instances of over-engineering**
- **8 new problems introduced by the revision**

The most blocking items are: the function-level inventory absence (2.1), the incomplete PHP-to-Python mapping (2.2), the charter-vs-ADR decision status contradiction (1.2/4.2), and the ADR filename mismatches in AGENTS.md (1.1).

```
### Migration Rules
6. Target Python code goes into `target-repos/` — this is where the migrated project grows
7. Every spec document in `specs/` must cross-reference source files by relative path (e.g., `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/db.php`) rather than duplicating source code
8. Specs may include **reasonable code examples** to highlight important architectural decisions, but must not be a copy of the source
9. When migrating, always verify behavior parity against the source spec before marking a component complete

### Source Traceability Rule (MANDATORY)
10. **Every meaningful code element** (function, class, method, model, route, constant) in `target-repos/` **MUST** have a traceability comment linking it to its PHP source origin. This is a hard constraint — code without traceability comments must not be committed.

    **Traceability comment format** (use the most specific match available):

    ```python
    # Source: ttrss/classes/feeds.php:Feeds::view (lines 45-120)
    def view_feed(feed_id: int, view_mode: str) -> dict:
        ...

    # Source: ttrss/include/functions.php:catchup_feed (lines 1094-1237)
    def catchup_feed(feed_id: int, cat_view: bool, ...) -> None:
        ...

    # Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton pattern)
    # Python equivalent: SQLAlchemy engine via Flask-SQLAlchemy extension
    db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)

    # Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_feeds, lines 38-72)
    class Feed(Base):
        __tablename__ = "ttrss_feeds"
        ...
    ```

    **Match levels** (use the most specific that applies):
    - **Direct**: `function → function` or `class → class` (e.g., `Feeds::view` → `view_feed()`)
    - **Method-level**: `Class::method` → Python method (e.g., `RPC::mark` → `rpc.mark_article()`)
    - **File-level**: When a Python module aggregates logic from a single PHP file (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/ccache.php`)
    - **Multi-file**: When a Python module synthesizes logic from multiple PHP files (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/functions.php + ttrss/include/functions2.php (query building)`)
    - **Schema-level**: For models derived from SQL schema (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_user_entries)`)
    - **Inferred**: When Python code has no direct PHP equivalent but was inferred from PHP patterns (e.g., `# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (session validation pattern, adapted for Flask-Login)`)
    - **New**: When code is genuinely new with no PHP source (e.g., `# New: no PHP equivalent (Alembic migration infrastructure)`)
```

    99→## Anti-Patterns to Avoid
   100→
   101→These are specific to patterns found in the TT-RSS PHP source:
   102→
   103→| Anti-Pattern | Why Dangerous | Mitigation |
   104→|-------------|---------------|------------|
   105→| Replicate `db_fetch_assoc` iteration pattern | Verbose, error-prone manual row iteration | Use SQLAlchemy result sets and ORM queries directly (ADR-0006) |
   106→| Replicate `$_SESSION` global access pattern | Untestable, hidden coupling | Use dependency injection or Flask `g` / Flask-Login `current_user` (ADR-0007) |
   107→| Replicate dual-DB SQL branches (MySQL + PostgreSQL) | Double testing burden, divergent behavior | PostgreSQL only (ADR-0003) |
   108→| Replicate `htmlspecialchars()` calls | Easy to miss, leads to XSS | Use Jinja2 autoescape (on by default) |
   109→| Replicate `functions.php` / `functions2.php` monolith | 3000+ line god-files, impossible to test | Split by domain: `feeds.py`, `articles.py`, `users.py`, etc. |
   110→| Replicate singleton pattern for `Db` / `PluginHost` | Hidden global state, blocks testing | Use Flask extensions and dependency injection (ADR-0010) |
   111→| Gold-plating during migration | Adding features breaks behavioral parity | Strict parity constraint (C3); improvements come after migration |
   112→| Frontend rewrite during backend migration | Two moving targets, compounding risk | Keep existing JS in Phase 1 (ADR-0004) |
```

## Assistant

Done. Source traceability is now a **hard constraint (C7)** enforced in three places:

1. **AGENTS.md Rule 10** — the full rule with format specification, 7 match levels (Direct, Method-level, File-level, Multi-file, Schema-level, Inferred, New), and code examples
2. **Project Charter C7** — hard constraint (violation = rejection)
3. **Traceability Matrix** — tracked requirement with status

Every function, class, method, model, and route in `target-repos/` must have a `# Source:` comment linking to the PHP origin. Match granularity goes from exact (`Class::method → function`) down to fuzzy (`# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (pattern adapted for Flask-Login)`), with `# New:` for genuinely novel code.
